O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear son, I have completed this book that is the essence of medical knowledge together with its fulfillment, and I have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete this treatise with you, which is part of the work by hand, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work by hand is practiced in our region and spread throughout everywhere, it is excellent in science and capability, and is not delayed from its force but only the small descriptions in books of the ancients that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, there has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed up, and science is removed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I can vivify this treatise together with the order of this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and will come together with the forms of the fire cautery, and other instruments of the work by means of the declaration and preparation of it, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for this reason, because there are no good hands masters found in our time, is the art of medicine extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who deals with it must master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as far as he knows the shape and arrangement and separation of the organs, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of bones, and the movement and flowing veins and resting veins, and their source.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, as Iopras says, what is done with the hands is not much, and what is done with work is little; and most of all in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the above-mentioned things should be careful so as not to fall into error and not to harm people; therefore, I have repeatedly warned many of those who deal with this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess on the throat of a woman, and he also cut the arteries in the throat; so much blood flowed that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who treated a stone in the bladder of a man, and the stone was big; he took out a piece of the bladder and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have also been called to treat it with a lever, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; and if he treated it properly, he would not die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who took a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was an injury; and the ignorant doctor pulled out the break onto the wound with a strong lever, leaving no scar on the wound, and left it like that; and he commanded that he not remove it; and he delayed so that the leg became completely deformed and the bones came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come to release the leg; and when I released it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all paths of corruption had already been established for the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member as long as the members were completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another miracle, that is, an abscess that was putrefied and then inflamed by the evil of its own nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chalc, when it is purred with melancholic humor, will not come to touch it unless it is in a favorable position where one can completely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, good sons, you should know that the work of the hands is divided into two divisions: namely, that in which there is danger and fear in many aspects; and I will show you in each of the things of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So that the poor man does not speak ill of you if he takes your weapons away from you, and so that you can take your patients lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are freed; and leave behind expected diseases of grief health; and remove your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiæn makes some of his admonitions: 'Do not take on yourself a bad disease for which you might be called a madman.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are fire cauterizations and medicinal water cauterizations, and the chapters are ordered from the top down to the bottom; and the shapes of instruments, and the ironings of cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	Si it is for cutting and piercing, and for suction cups and wounds, and for extracting arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar things; and it is arranged with respect to the head as much as possible, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work; it is necessary that I give the quality of the aid and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the most distant word and subtle science and the secret answered; and many sages would speak of it, and agree to this; and I am satisfied with a few words, for I shorten the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that aid cautery is universal to all colors or materials, except for two colors; that is, a color that has heat and a material, and a color that is dry and a material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry mixture of substances, neither agreed nor said that cautery is great help; and the other said the opposite: that cautery is not worth it for illness that comes from heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by hot disease from heat or drought; and he who said that cautery is great help for hot and dry diseases that come to the body's core.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have not found it once by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And any way, only he who has experienced it, and who knows by long practice the properties of cautery, and the diversity of complexions in men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies, and space of time; we do not fear other complexions, even if they have cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all this should come together and agree with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery will help in healing if there are secretions and of greater good than medicinal fire cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it comes only to the member that is cooked, and it does not harm another member in any way.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The medicinal fire comes from one member to another by moving away, and causes diseases of great healing; and because of its height and its substance's goodness it does not cause it, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And which I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and is based on the truth of things; and because of this I apologize for the length of speech, for it does not please me that I should keep you from the secret that is answered in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases of bodies, as the philosopher says in proving; so accept it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made at certain times and be performed with prayer.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, for because the harm caused by the aid of cauterization is sometimes prevented; and most importantly, the cauterization is done for necessary and urgent pains that cannot be put up with until such time as a greater malady comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, dear son, as some people do; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they think, because cauterization is nothing more than a medicine that changes the appearance, dries up the humors that cause pain, and does more good than medicine due to its speed in action, and because of its virtues and greatness of effect.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes according to the constitution of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of meat and similar things, unless cauterization is administered at the place where he has a little superfluity and moisture, as cauterizing with heat for pain, and similar things, and partial pain does not return but it is little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And few people understand because cauterization is called the bloodletting of medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are wrong, and cauterization is the bloodletting of medicine because when we administered ways to treat diseases in any disease and they did not work, then let us administer the cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauterization is the bloodletting of medicine, not according to the intention of the foolish, but
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Li ancien dirent que cauteres d'estrument d'or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualité de l'or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n'est mie voir car je l'ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c'est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d'or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	The ancient said that gold cauterization instruments are less corrosive than those of iron, and they only mentioned the quality of gold and its high purity; they said that the heat of the gold cauterization instrument does not cause inflammation, but it is not true because I have tested it, and I found that it is true in some people; and gold cauterization instruments are more durable than those of iron, as they say. However, when you heat the gold instrument, you do not know when it is too hot, and it may catch fire; and thus there is sufficient prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you may order this chapter of the heart to be read just as soon as possible, so that the vision may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery is good for a moisture and cold on the skull, and because of many humors that descend from the head through the hair, and through the ears, and for many dreams and pain in the teeth and pain in the throat, and especially for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and lameness and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged with a soothing medicine that washes out the head three or four times, according to what the virtue and the sharpness and the habit of the patient can bear; and then wash the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the cross between your hands, and put his hands on his chest; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of its neck between its II eyes; and if it comes to you, let the blood flow first, then heat the cautery that is called "olive", from which comes this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the ink signet, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little turning it over; then release your hand slowly, and cover the bone with a little thread; and if you do not see it, start again with the cautery as I told you; after that, take a little thread, and put soft cotton inside, and place it on the ink, and let it be for III days; after that, put wet cotton in butter; and let it be until the bone is heated; then cure the wound of the ointment which is called "tetrafarmacon" until it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old man said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it festers; and for this reason, if it is treated immediately.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one should let the fire cautery burn so long that a part of the bone is burned, and then resect what is burned from the bone, and be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another one said that one should let the fire cautery burn so high and so hard that it exposes the bone as much as possible to allow the humors to exit; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after which, one must heal and mend.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem good to me in all cases, except that in some people where there is a risk of death; and it seems to me that I should let them be, because the shoulder joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness with other members; and moreover, when the shoulder joint of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first impression of cauterization seems more safe and mild to me, and from which I use to assemble in a way that saves life.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the child's pain at the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the whole head begins to ache chronically and for a long time, then one should use yernises and pills which are called 'coches', and head-washing with oils and plasters; and if one makes the fire cautery as we have described above, it will help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize it slightly as we have described above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After making the fire cautery over each of the patient' head bones as we have described above, and making the cautery at the base which is called 'vassellez', and putting the wind-cups; and align your hand so that you do not see the bone: the pain in this cautery is much greater than in the others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary for the cauterization of the horns to be finer than that of which we make the cautery on the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head there is sudden pain and it goes up to the oil, and the head has been purged with medicines that harm, and all this does not help: then let the fire cautery be made according to two ways, that is to say, with water medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The fire cautery, if it is that you squeeze a bunch of aloes, and peel the bark and wrap it around the head at the place where the pain is, and then make a temple or bandage with it so that you can put the aloe on the skin; and when it has been wrapped for twelve hours, then untie it and dip the aloe in oil, and leave the wound covered for two or three days; then put cotton in oil to wrap it up until it is ready.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment as long as he is healthy; and if you see that this medicine burns, then take half of what I have written in my book on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if it is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer with this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it 'clos' because the head is made in the form of a clo or it has I pit of curve, and to the middle there is an little appearance; and place it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, so that the half of the nail is burned; and remove your hand that the artery does not burn, which is sore, and runs abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After place cotton in wool, and place it on the place for III days; then I put cotton wet in butter, and then cure the place with ointment as long as he is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cauterizer which is called 'cultellare', at all the tip, and keep yourself from covering the artery in this headache that is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	For migraine, if you follow what we have said before in the division of diseases, and don't profit from it, and see that the cauterization with the fire does not suit him at all, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called 'cultellare' until it is white; and sign so on the pain a line of half an inch long, and hold your hand once, and pull out that you do not cover the artery and do not come up to the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when one bites, and let there be no rustling or spasms in the migraine, and beware of the escape of blood from the artery when it is cut, or when a copement has great fear and more importantly for him who does not know it, and who is students and proven; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop the pain when the artery is cut, and I will show you at what point it happens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him with fire at the top of his head as well, and cure the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapister for extracting an artery, with the cautery that has II blades; and this cautery is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	for the pain of ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ears comes from cold, and medicine or other treatments we mentioned in the division do not help, then this cautery which is called "poins" should be used, whose form is:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying "poins" all around the painful ear, or around both ears where the pain is, and moving away a little from the root of the ear then that you have marked the place; and there are X points around each ear; after that, cure the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated by cautery is only effective for those that move with fluid, as we have said in the division of illnesses; and not to make any cauterization for the similitudes that come from seborrhea and scales of fish.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this torture of the mouth that moves with fluid, seborrhea, and scalp conditions and gargling, and so on, it is appropriate to make three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, another a little further down the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and place the cautery in the part that is healthy, and let it burn for half of the time; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the image of the cutler that we have put before you, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the knives are a little more thick; after care let the place be as I said before, until he is well.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauterizations: II on the II horns of the head, and I cut off the head, and I put in it what is called a 'vessel', as we have said before, and a cauterization after the stomach mouth; and let it be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	of limestone
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	This is a disease that requires many years of treatment and gives the patient pills to rub on the brain; after re-shaping the head of the patient, put on the scalp a plaster of mustard which is written or prepared plasters; and this is the way of the cauterization: do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healthy then it is good; and if not, he makes three cauterizations on the top of the head down to the collarbone, and leaves a space between each cauterization of two inches in length; and the surgeon performs them as with others, and when they see that he is shaking, the patient suffers, so one cauterization is made in the middle; and if it is necessary, two others are made on either side, and the surgeon continues to cauterize until he is healthy; and let the cauterizations which are called "olive-color" be made as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	Let the head be washed and cleaned as we have said before; then, with a sharp knife, he makes a cut on the top of the head and around each ear, and one behind and three on the back of the neck; and if it is necessary to do so, and the neck is moist and the patient suffers and becomes worse, then he makes four cauterizations on the spine of the neck; and he leaves them until the second scar is burnt, and he stops; after that, the surgeon continues to treat him until he is healthy, and let the cauterizations which are called "olive-color" be made as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	For the fire cautery, one should only use it on those who are feverish, and first moisten the scalp and perform other treatments we have mentioned in the chapter on treatment when the patient is severe and suffering from heat-based medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If it is a child who cannot tolerate this, make them gargle and chew, moisten the scalp regularly with good meat; then place the liquid in the middle of the head, and perform the cautery according to what we have said above, and also cauterize on the neck, and on each horn; and if the patient is extremely ill and suffering, perform the cautery as I have said before for those who are paralyzed and have a soft body, on the spine of the back and neck, and make the olive cautery according to the manner that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is blind, then perform the fire cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excesses or corrupt moisture and thick fluid, then lou cauterize partly with the fire cautery as we have said to one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the excesses decline into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then he drinks something to cleanse the brain, according to what has been said in the division about it.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After putting the head of the patient; then make a turban of fine linen, also as a circle, put it on the head; and let the patient sit in a good position and be held fast from all sides; then present the liniment, and rub with old shea butter; and heat the fire moderately, so that he may suffer it; after which empty the circle out through the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient every week once with another good governance, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And if you see fire cautery, make many punctures all over the cauterization.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This way of cauterizing moistens the skull, increased; and then put cotton wet in wax and in linseed oil on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes first the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do drink to the patient a thing purifying the skull, and warding away all moisture, and let it sweat or bathe many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he has commanded to re-open his skull, and he makes a fire cauterization on the skull, and he makes II cauterizations on the II temples because there is loss of sight in both eyes, or one of them is lost; and cope with all cauterization the veins and arteries that are dislocated, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple; and ward against blood coming out, and if you see too much blood flowing, then stop it with a cloth as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and with cauterization how to stop bleeding; and no one makes cauterization or hemolysis of the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	The two courses of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or remove the arteries that are in appearance of the head outward; and one can see that it is of the cold and phlegmatic excess, then he makes the cauterization that I said at the beginning of the awed descending to the eyes: I cauterize the top, and II cauterizes on the two temples, and II cauterizes where it haters the two bones; and if it is necessary more, if he cauterizes bloodlessly over the socket, then do one small cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The two courses of tears move inward through the eyes.
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevais; et te warde de l'artere que tu ne la coper.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called “clavis”:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery of this cautery that is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	for this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you do two cauteries on the two sorcs as long as the sorcs are; and you leave the hand off until as much as the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	dou poil qui point l’oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No hair has ever turned to oil, nor has it touched the oil, and yet on it have been performed two kinds of cauterization: namely, fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and equal in length, then place the patient on your table; after that, sign on the paper of the eyes a figure which is also like the furrow of the mirror, and this is the beginning of the sign to remove the hairs; then put cotton wet with balm and musk on the oil, and then heat the cautery so that it has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cauterized the affected area little by little several times, so that the scar is burned at the spot; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand up to the point where the oil is; then gently lower your hand, and leave it like this for III days, then put cotton soaked in oil in a sack until the burn is healed; after the wound has been treated so that it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come, and the paper is softened then start again with the cautery in the middle as you did before; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper returns to its natural position, and is even, and does not touch the hair with the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medicinal fire cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a shape of parchment in the form of an oak leaf; then take French soap and hot water, each half a cup, and grind them together well; and do it quickly, so that it does not cool down again, then spread it on the parchment shapes; and if the disease is only in one oil spot, then one must be applied in one, and also in both, and put cotton soaked in oil in an oven; and the patient's cheek shall be in your healthy hand and place your two fingers on the medicine, and press it little by little each time the patient feels the tingling of the medicine, for he will feel the tingling as well as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	If you have had this for a long time, take the medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blister has passed, lift up the flap, and you will see if the paper is lifted as it was lifted by the fire or by incision; and if so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, continue with the medicine on the spot where the blister has not opened, as long as your hairs are even and your wounds clean; then put cotton wetted in vinegar on the sore place, after which cure the sore which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have to take care of your wound with great care so that the medicine does not touch the hairs.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft after that, and the hair pricks into the oil, start again the medicine on that very spot which has become soft from the paper properly, in the same way as you have done before; after curing it until it heals; and this is the form of the blister of the skin:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and shape, according to their nature; and do not therefore adopt for those who are subject to your instruction the same method as is used in this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not benefit them, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and dip the scalp (in a) cotton soaked in oil or juice of persimmon on oil; then heat the cautery until it is hot; and put the cautery on the scalp as if it were the shape of a feather; together, the point should be applied to one spot, so that you do not burn the skin by accident, but rather as if it were a tent; nevertheless, be careful that it does not burn the hair.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula is opened and treat porriture and dry it; and if it is closed, then work, and firmly treat the bow; after put on the hot cauterizer, and hold your hand at the cauterizer to the part next to the oil from behind, so that your hands do not go crazy; and put the cauterizer in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of cauterization just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then begin cauterization again, and if you need more, leave it for three days; after put cotton wet in grease, and cure the drying of the infection as long as it is healthy, and if forty days pass and it is not healthy, then put on medicine that corrodes the bone; and treat according to what came out in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have a way of cauterizing fistulas, which no one of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Heard it, and found the place; after, put in the narrow thread of which this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I do so in the quantity of one third of a pound; and hold your hand firmly, so that the melted oil does not run to his eye; and it comes that you put the oil to the patient's cotton wetted at the bottom of a jar or a pot: The oil thus artfully applied to the place of the fistula, and the health is restored by a wonderful cure.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization which we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	But if not, then a piece of iron should be administered to the nose, and the fistula brought back to the nose's own place according to what should be done in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	crevasses in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	times have creases in the lips, which are called "hair", and most often in the lips of adults.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these creases as we have said in the divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then heat a small caustice according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it immediately in the creases until it comes out clean; then treat it with the ointment until it is well.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When abscess comes in the root of the throat or the palate or the roots of the teeth, after having made porriture and rot and it becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, but it does not benefit: then you should have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after having opened or pierced the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron comes up to the bottom of it, and do so once or twice, after treating it as we have said in the treatment, until it is well; and if it is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, then you should uncover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and this does not work, then put the head of the sick person in your lap; then heat the cautery until its form comes out in such a way that you put a string on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside, and hold your hand so that the sick person feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then release your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; then fill the mouth of the sick person with dirty water, and let it sit for an hour and rinse it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In such a way that the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the gums that were softened are dried up, and the moisture that corrupts is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is coldness or numbness, and medicines do not help, then you have to use two types of cauterization: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	If the cauterization is to be done with fire, make a metal or bronze rod thick enough that the flame does not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery so that it cools down as you apply it to the tooth, and hold your hand there until it has cooled; do this often, for the pain will become bearable the next day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the hurry of this cauterization, and then take it away quickly. And thus is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a wound in the nose that you want, and according to what you can do; and this is the form of the knife:
des scrophules	from the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of cold damp and does not submit to digestion by medicines, then heat the head of the shoulder with fire so that it comes after the form, and has two openings for the fumes to rise from the cauterization on the other side; and place the cautery hot on the abscess once, where it needs to be, until it reaches the root of the abscess; and put cotton wet with butter on it as long as the burning is done; after that cure with oil and poultices until it is well.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails over the chin, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then the patient should be voided first by giải thuốc giải độc; after that, make cauterization at the root of the throat, and keep yourself from going further than the throat, and dare not cut but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, make another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cauterization which is called 'clavicle' be the form before us; and heal the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of cold are due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or itching, and it is an old disease, then make him iij cauterizations on the forearm in his veins; and another cauterization at the base of the penis between the testicles; and let the cauterizations which are called 'clavicle' according to the form which is before us said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make a fire-cauterization on all the cauterizations that are called "poins" of which the form is as mentioned above in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or so around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, treat the hole according to what is mentioned above, and let the cauterization be made with three rains according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for those where the cauterization is lighter, for which you make three together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, have the patient lie on his back and on his side; then feel with your right hand the nape, where the joint is dislocated; and if the joint is dislocated inward, make the cauterization that has two nubs as mentioned above in this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize him until he pierces it as close to the coast as possible, and comes out with the figure of the cautery together with three cauteries; and because this is made with the cautery that has three nerves, so that the figure of the cauterization are there three cauteries; and the nerve according to the subtility of a tent and it is the shape of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never place on this nerve because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After that, place the ring of fire on it; then let the patient rest, and do not move his limbs for a long time until he is well established.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated again, let the following thing happen; then make a cauterization with the thick ring of fire, or a large number of cauteries pierce it.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is dried up, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach there come chills and moisture until it is removed from its color, and are multiplied to him the catharres, and are manners of accustomed cures and he does not benefit, then the patient should be made to lie on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Therefore after him do III cauterions I of the cow's milk by the quantity of a two, all cauterions are nailed, and II cauterions later on both sides as long as the form of the cauterions is at III angles, and there is space between them so that they are not joined together when they go on fire; and be the cauterion so perfect that it scorches both parts, and is the form of the cauterions according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize your stomach with a large cautery according to this form; and the one who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by piercing and signing on the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you desire to cut; then cauterize at all the cautery which is called 'point'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the wound that we had before, as long as he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	Regarding the liver, when it has pain from cold and moisture and strong windiness, as long as it is forcibly removed from its natural composition due to excesses; and the patient is treated for what we have said in the divisions, and it does him no good, unless he becomes sour on his back; and the sign of the incision is three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, removing the hypocondries where the knife of the ombel comes; and leave a space between each cautery of two inches; and let the cautery of the long neck of the torso, and do not press much with your hand at all the cautery; and let it be burned with great heat halfway through; and let the patient lie on his back; and if he cannot, then let him extend his legs, and raise his breasts; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is, then cauterize these cauterices of the cuttle, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all of it, for you would make the whole body dry; and let it come to no more than a bean's eye, for the cautery is very subtle in this place, and it is small to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you can tell whether it is in the parenchyma of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the parenchyma, then feel that the patient feels little pain; but if it is in the capsule, then feel severe pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then, when this treatment of the blisters has finished, let the patient be careful on his head; and then sign with your finger where the abscess is, and then heat the fire which resembles the root, from which this shape comes:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I the cautery until the curings be burnt, and come to syphac, until the porreture be all furished; after the cure according to the cure of sweates as long as it be sane; and there is no need but of this cautery use none furishes but those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by which hands these diseases have never been corrupted any time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And then it can take hard work, and always I think that we should leave him.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the plaudits of pleurisy:
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	For the plaudits of pleurisy: The ancients said that one should make cauterizations with roots of aristolochia, and in a similar way: take a root of aristolochia that is long, the largest you can find, and dry it, and make it also as thick as your two fingers; and soak it in oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize between the lobe and the chin, and make four small cauterizations descending into the part which is sore on the beard; and make a cauterization between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly behind a little; and I cauterize emmi the breast, and I another over the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and one along the back from the breast; and do not press your hand, but rather open it widely as when you smell.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no ancient said that any man use fire cautery resembling a razor, and scrape and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the apex; and leap out of pain, so as we have said in the apex of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient will die now, or a fistula comes from which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse, as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then they have three ways of fire cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
