Of these three ways, one way is that you make three cauterizations, or four, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the fire cautery of the liver which we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient sweat on his back; and another way of cauterization is that you heat the cautery which has two ners, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and place the cautery which is place of the mouse, or where the cut comes from towards the left, and are the elevations which you feel by the touch, according to the length of the body, and the cauterization be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After placing the two wands in fire until the sound of one can be heard from the other side, and then quickly treat with the cautery, and so on. And if you see it, cauterize to the whole with three wands.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure has gotten worse over a long time, and this is true that the other before said cure must be used.
de ydropisie	dyropisie
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery does not suit yropic, except for the way that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat according to the ways we have mentioned in the divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is appropriate that you make four cauterizations around the boude, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the kidney, and two behind the back on the spine, and one place the pis; and let the cauterization be close to the cure.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After remove the fire cautery to go away long-lasting scorching, and do not leave the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing would hurry, and both intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the fire cautery for the abdomen is the clave that we have before us most frequently; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is herebefore described.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of the parts
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the parts are swollen in one who is hydropic, and are pale yellow in color, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the index and middle fingers; and gently lift up your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep in the part, otherwise it would come out white; and make the cauterization according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing the fire cautery on both legs up to the tip of the knife; and let the cautery be long, one behind the knee in front and the other behind, between the leg; and leave the cauteries a long time without healing, that the wound goes away; after healing the others as we said.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the abdomen comes from cold and moisture, as long as the digestive and beneficial qualities remain in the stomach and the intestines are afleboied, and cannot be healed by any means; and you see the patient suffering much and of great strength, so do I make a great fire cautery on the stomach according to what he has talked about before or the cautery of the stomach, circulating; and four cauteries around the navel very finely, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see moisture abundant and the patient suffering, then make fire cautery on his knuckle, and I cautery on each finger, and II small cauteries in the stomach of the great, for the remedy is profitable when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	For the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the root, or one or more, and are old and have large cold wet腐敗humors, and are cured as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit, then do fire cautery: III on the spine of the back, that which is all outside let it be cut little by little in a triangle, and I cauterize outside the two bowels; and if you think that his stomach is cold, and the meat does not cook, and one sees swelling on the face, then the face let it have a large cautery as said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse at all cauterized clavicle; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Aftercare until he is healthy again.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	from the charnosity which is called “theloële”
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you treat the charnosity, if it is hot, the fire cautery that seems like a razor, and then put it all ablaze on the treated area; and let it rest as much as your hand can manage so that the cauterization reaches the birth of the vein, from which it will not move; do this once or twice, and if there is more charnosity, cauterize each one as we have said; after treating with beneficial ointments until they are healthy again; and if you cauterize a large area with a large cautery, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	from a wound that has not been treated well
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will tell you in your place, if it comes to a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is no outlet for the vent, and it is inflamed and produces pus and corruption, then you should provide a complete thin paste, and be sure to know exactly how much of the paste is required.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery that seems like a razor, and pouring it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and restart the cautery as many times as there is corruption and pus, once or three times, according to the quantity required; and be careful not to damage the nerves that are underneath, and open large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula runs to the belly and intestines, then be careful of these veins, and do not cut them except in their charn, and know that they are not useless; after healing the vein as long as it is healthy, and if the veins have been severed, and the matter has become hard for a long time, then know that the vein is completely healed; and if the matter has not become hard, know that the vein is three-quarters healed, and the bone is corrupted at its root; and thus, as one of these that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of the kidneys and the great wind comes, and does not take a woman's shape, then it is necessary that you make a cauterization on the kidneys from one side to the other at the clavicle cautery which we have just said; and if we cauterize ourselves in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and greater help will be done.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from fever and moisture, so that the patient retenes urine, then you make a cauterization on the back of the bladder, where the hair of the penis comes out, and one on each side, as long as we do it with a nail; and you make another cauterization behind, where you need to do so; and make the clavicle cautery according to the shape mentioned before.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow it to conceive, and the flowers are rotten and delayed in their growth; and when they come, then great pain is felt: so three caustic treatments should be applied around the buttocks, as we have said for the cautery of the bladder, and two treatments lower down the back; and let the treatments be claved, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends into the hip joint box, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the sign is that the thigh is farther away than the other when measured together; and the joints are found deep, then you should apply a seemingly circular cautery to the sick person on the hip joint box, and mark before the joint around the box as it turns, so that the box is inside the circle; and if so, apply the treatments like those with which we have cauted the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery does not present itself to you, do three cauterizations of the olive-sized granulation, and let the cauterizations be completely done like all the curings; and heal as long as he is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the knee
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When the pain comes in the box of the knee, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is appropriate that you purge the patient of the large humors with foul pills, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, make the cauterization; and the manner of the cauterization is according to two manners: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization is according to many manners, of which one is this: that you cauterize on top of the box of the knee three triangular cauterizations according to this form, and make it deep and large, and leave between each cauterization a space the size of two, and let the cauterizations be olive-sized; never do you make a cauterization in the middle on top of the head of the knee, for there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cautery at the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in a different way so that the circles contain all the hip, and all the flesh of the knee is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain extends to the thigh and leg, then make two cauterizations at the place where the patient feels the pain, and one on top of the ankle, two on the left leg; and either make the cauterization with a knife, or burn the flesh of the knee; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or almost there, then cauterize at the spot where he feels the pain, three points or four at the cauterization called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he is working, do more; and if it is known that the pain is coming from the knee toward the thigh, he does a fire cautery with a cut-out or round knife, and you give him good warning in all your cauterizations that you do not let go so much of the cauterization that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause more injury and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have done a cauterization on the heel of the foot and left it so long that the leg went completely limp, and the toes as well, and became pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly which he had, he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two places together, do a cauterization on each one, according to this way.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sage said in the cauterization of the hip, so this is the way, make it one large and thick as a thumb knuckle, or a little less, and space between each one the quantity of a nut of peas; and the indentations are on both sides, and they are also like thumbs, and there is one piece of iron well made; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	And heat it until it is completely red and dry, and then put it on the box of the bad hip, and turn it over the healthy ribs; and cauterize once I cauterize and leave three days; and then make an ointment of butter, and leave the open wound long; after the cure of dressing as long as it is healthy.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	Albucasis says that we use little of this cauterization because of the fear of its regrowth, and few know who use it; but surely it is a good cauterization, which can tolerate it, and where it sticks.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After resting on the chest of the patient who is lying on his back, and quickly put your hand up to the hip; then get between the two circles of hot awl which are heated by fire one pot, and leave it an hour before suffering the pain and heat of the patient.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is true that the burn also happens like fire; and when the burns are passed, take your hand away from the instrument and lift the hip with soft awl, and leave it thus for three days, and put on butter as long as the scorching is white; and let it be for three days to heal; and that one behind will help after the treatment of oils until he is well.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends only to the thigh or only to the leg, make the awl hot according to what you have done in the hip more; and this is the way of hot awl, and I have written it or doctor of correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and live chisel, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a nine pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Take a small hole somewhere that the point of one needle can fit through; and place that pot on top of another well-plumbed pot, and put the alkali and chisel and soft water on it, until there are two layers of powder on top; then leave it like this until it has dried up a little water and dust; then take all that water, and pour it over the chisel and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then if it is very wet and has dried out in the preparation of medicinal remedies and other cauterizations; because it does the same work as fire, and with other medicines, where one cauterizes well with honey, acacia, and soap, all these things are mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Gallien us tells a cure wherein one honourable was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and he made much murmur, and said that another cure was not done, and that he was healed all at once when this cure was made, and he bathed himself as it is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he said in this way that you squeeze the green and dry marble, and crush it with a little fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and let it be; and leave it for III hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter or bath as long as his body is a little aroused, and let him enter the bed, and the pain will go away all and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery of such medicines, unless after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And 디아スコ리데스 says that when the sciatic vein is burned with a goat's horn, it helps much; and the cautery must be made in such a way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take another and burn it with oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb of the foot and the other which is called the fistula.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take a dry goat' horn, and hold it in fire until it becomes charcoal, and lay it on the wool, and leave it until it is blackened; and do this again, and never cease to do so as long as you think that it comes to the knee, and the pain ceases; and this way of cauterizing is called "cauterize de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	from the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or from چرور، یا توسط ضربه یا از طریق تخلیه زیاد، یا از شباهت ماده ی سرد گسترش یافته، هیچ یک از این شباهت ها ارزش cauteering ندارند، مگر اینکه آنهایی که از infusions of cold material come.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	He should after that the sick person is voided of foul pills or others, that one does to him on the back, where the pain remains, three lines of two inches long, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the virtue and the quantity that the sick can bear; and let be done the cauterization according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do III cauteries or IIII at the cautery with key according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Often this disease comes to small children, and the signs of onset are that they have tight back when they stand up and are afraid; and you will find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes on top of the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this person and you see him heal, if he is cauterized with the cautery of that one according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery is equally applied to each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, so cauterize inside the spine with the piercing cautery two lines or three, and let the punctures be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards, heal the area as much as it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery in gibbosity which is in the spice of nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints' pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture that spreads to each limb, and when the pain comes in pieces, which is called "podagre" properly, and when it is of a cold cause and cannot be cured with medicine, then it is cured with cauterization in this way: make the cautery's juice around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary for you to hold the foot, then make a fire cautery with all the fire cauteries that are claimed "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make a fire cautery on each knee III cauterization or IIII of each part, with all the olive cauterization; and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand firmly except for as long as the skin of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains go down to the knees and back, administer the cauterization that we have spoken about in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, then make a hole of II lines; and if there is still pain in the two, then make a fire cautery on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the arms or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and govern the patient well and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do this with good government and you purge the fluid, then you will be healed by God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syph
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in anger, and the bile descends as the bowels move, it is new, so that when you look at him, he should not go out that day; and use things that cool his belly, so that the end descends from his belly; after let him sit on his back between your hands, and order him to shave his hair as long as his bile is repaired, and bring it to your feet, and sign a half circle above his body from the back of the hand, and at all times that is similar to half a circle; then heat the cautery in which there is this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it pours drops.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then put the balls back in place; and the minister will hold his hand so that they do not turn back; and well operate on the legs of the patient, and put a cloth and an apron on him, and another on his feet that holds his hands; then put the cautery on his ankle at all your hand, and keep it firm and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, begin again another time until you come to the bone; and be careful so that the ball does not slip when you are operating with the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that through this, the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauterization of children be subtle according to their size, and for adults as well according to their size; after III days cure the site of the cautery with butter until it is warmed up; after that cure other remedies until he is healthy, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be kept in place for a long time, so that the ball does not slip when he wants to go to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, a well-made bandage is brought to him and changed every four days; and he has good rest, that he works little and guards against too much drinking and eating, and too loud noise; and when he has done this teaching, he is completely cured.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of the cutter in his paste.
de la routure dou ventre	from the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are not getting better, you will see that they no longer grow; you make the fire cautery according to its quantity, and burn it on the third day of the cure; after the cure according to what we have said; and no one of the old ones said that it should be fire-cauterized on three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is the place of incision and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another below it, and with your hand press all the fire-cauterized part.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any member, or from a knock or a wound, and this pain persists for a long time, and medicine does not help, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cauldron which is called 'poins', and the cauterization according to the length of the limb, its smallness, its weakness, its virtue, and its location from twists, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed after the first cauldron, that is good; but if not, then go back and apply another cauldron to that very same spot, for this is the custom: you must apply the cauldron as long as the patient remains unhealed.
de meselerie	of mischief
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The misfortunes are alleviated by cauldron in no way or to a great degree, and most often the disease comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Et si la melaurie est partout espare; et elle perd manifestement, il convient que tu les cauterises de ces cauteres que nous avons dit ou chef, et un cautere en som lou neis, et deux cauteres sur l'espinee dou col, et six cauteres sur l'espinee dou dos, et un grand sur la crupie et un autre deliez, et deux sur les deux espaules; et deux sur les coutes, et deux sur les tendrons dou pis, et un sur chascune jointure des mains et des pieds, et sur les fosses des mains; et garde-toi des nerfs qui sont sous le derrien calcant, que tu ne les brules; et ne fais jamais aucun cautere sur l'os du poignet, et un autre sur l'os de l'estomac, et un autre sur le foie.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And if the melaria is everywhere sparse; and it loses manifestly, it is necessary that you cauterize them with these cauterizes that we have said at the head, and one cauterize in som lou neis, and two cauterizes on the spine of the neck, and six cauterizes on the spine of the back, and one great one on the crupie and another deliez, and two on the two espaules; and two on the shears, and two on the tendrons of the pis, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fosses of the hands; and keep away from the nerves that are under the derrien calcant, so you do not burn them; and never do any cauterize on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver. And know that when I make more cauterizes, I make more help, and move it to profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain at the cauterize as those who are healthy do, because the body is already very corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the way of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, cure with flour of times with honey and other cures as long as he is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swelling comes to any member and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not yet healthy, then do the cauterization on the member according to its greatness and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little bit entering into the flesh of the cure; then treat with ointments until he is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And no time is done cauterizing and by hand and by foot and by back, at the exit of the nerve that mute the member, and so if it is a bone; and nevertheless it does not matter if there are no knowledge of the limbs and exits of moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of armor
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the disease called "albaras" is present and the medicine is ineffective, then cauterize slightly with a fire cauldron according to the quantity of the medicine, until the blush is removed and its color changes; then cure it with flour of beans and lentils with oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of lamb and blood of pigeon, each part separately; and mix them all together, and bind them with a bandage, and apply to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for leprosy by cauterization:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the leprosy comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, if the cautery is made with a fire cauldron that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the leprosy.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	However, some say that cauterization should also be done in the middle of the leprosy; but I do not find this good, because I fear that it will become ulcers and rotten, and I have never seen it come to anything good; rather, it is better to cauterize all around, with the cauldron called "circle", as we have said in most of the cauldron.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it takes a long time to die, or because of the excess fluid produced by the disease, or because the person is very old and has little blood, or because they are very hungry; then you will see that the disease hastens the death: so cauterize them with small fire in poking; then leave them like that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that the whole body is being poked with fire, then heat the fire of this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of the disease called "adubelati" as long as the fire has pierced the pulse, and make such fires that the patient feels heat in some way so that the course of corruption is slowed.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After treatment as long as he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cure
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another form of disease that is called "corrosion," and is nothing other than a member's putrefaction, for it gnaws away at the members just as dry fire eats away at dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in its early stages that can be treated with fire, then heat the claves (incisions) small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the disease is; after treating with fire all around until it is completely corrupted, and nothing of it remains but only what has been corrupted, then all that is corrupted should be exposed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put oil on the incisions that are hurting from the heat until the burns from the fire have healed over, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of onions causing fever.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that chaps do not heal, it is good; and if they do not, begin the cauterization on those who are delayed from their places corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this medication is never cured of the fever by medicine in place of fire cauterization; but nevertheless, fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of fever by medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of onions that come to toes
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	times have passed that the feet by accidents give birth to a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large, troublesome thing that breaks the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to be understood cauterization by fire, and cauterization by hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautery with fire: if you heat cautery like a quill of vulture, and is made of good iron at the measure that it can bore the nail from all sides, and has subtle edges; after putting it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it comes to its base; and leave it in this way for III days as it begins to move corruption; then he makes a poultice of wild marigolds crushed with string, and leaves the poultice on all night, and the nails will come out and be uprooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound by dressing it every day until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if the body is converted by defizers, and many times hurt and cut, it is necessary that you apply hot water to it; and this is a good way: take a wire of iron or gold, or a quill of vulture, and put it on the nail and the pus, that is to say, to rot ulcers; and put the wire on it so that it rots all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and turn your hand many times so that the edge of the wire comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water's way deep until the root; and allow the patient a little of the burning sensation of the hot water for an hour; then leave it, and it will come out completely at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And so do another one, until you have drained all those who are in the heart, then cure the wounds that cause fury.
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shiver from cold, or from the quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and a cauterization at the feet, and one over the stomach with olive oil; this will stop the shivering, and will hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	the pustules that swell
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Once the skin breaks out in pustules that come from corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	if it is necessary at the first when they appear that you make a cauterization on each head of the pustule: a fine cauterization with oak bark, which is taken from the fire, or with the root of a long-hair grass, or with a lenticular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time are they cauterized at the beginning when they appear in this way, according to this method, and they cannot grow enquirers before, but the excess is broken which they bring, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are often great convulsions of blood from the artery that is cut off at the wound that comes to the surface, or when incising an abscess, or when cauterizing a limb, and similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stop bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever there is one [artery], then hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it as much as the blood stops with your finger, and no drop of it comes out; then take fire-olive [oil] with several small and large drops as much as it is all red; then take I, or a great or a little according to the wound and its place, and hold the cauterizer on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cauterizer on it until the blood stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if he seizes a fire when you feel your second pain in the vein, and the cautery is finished, if you take another cautery that are on fire quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other as long as the blood is stopped; and guard against burning the nerve that is delicate, and let no other evil come upon the patient; and know that when the artery is cut short from the vein, you can not stop it well yourself if the artery is large, except by one of the four ways we have mentioned: or by cauterizing, or by extraction when it has not yet been treated, or by firmly tying a thread, or by medicines put on it that have power to stop the blood; and bind and stretch it wisely.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer a tight bandage or place burning things on it, or similar things, if it does not benefit, then do not do it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to anyone and he has neither seen nor heard of medicine, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch them well over the wound and over the vein; and do not move him, but moisten his cold often, so that it is always cold and frozen and hardened and stuck to the wound; and make a scar in front of that from which he needs cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures for diseases related to the body's joints and muscles.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases related to fire, or burning medicine, and the pliers and causes and instruments and shapes of cauterization; and I put that ointment on the head of the shoulder until it reaches the tip, and I will go in this chapter through this middle path for those who suffer more lightly than others.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, since I have begun to speak of this, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of the cauterizations, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake madness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in this way people come to their end.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have destroyed themselves so that they die easily because of the foolishness of their disease, and of the greatness of their wickedness, then we must be afraid of them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from these signs, and he says: "Wait, I am pregnant"; and the disease is mocking.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to these who come to you who have this manner, but put more great courtesy in your honor than in your covetise, and do not open foolishly but carefully of him whom you are certain, and of whom you might have taken and lost; and use divination and indication in the treatment of your sick so that health may be converted; and he who will help to obtain good fame, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords grant you good understanding and justice, and if you will ask for the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in devising by chapters, according to the one that is before or the chapter of the cauterization, which I have devised from the chief to the tip, so that you may find more easily that of which you will have need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	dou chief plein d’aigue
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	I know that this disease often occurs in infants and when the baby cries too much, the head of the child is drawn tight; and there is never a response to this cause that we know of.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in infants, and all those that I have seen it in, it has brought about death soon after; and for this reason it seems to me that I should be less anxious about the work of this chapter in the treatment of these.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was all swollen with moisture, and the head became heavy every day so that it could not be held up; and the moisture was so great that it seemed to me that he would die, and this moisture gathered between the skin and the bone, between the neck and the bone; and the work of this chapter is such that if the moisture gathers between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a wide slit in the head with the knife; and let it be as far apart as we showed you, until the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the splint:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If the moisture has penetrated the bone, and the signs you see are the creases of the chin overlapping on each side, and the liquid jumps out when you press it with your hand from inside, and does not go back in: then you should make three incisions along the chin according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, remove the bandages and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave it for five days; then clean it with tendons and olive oil, and let the head be dried out equally, and give the patient dry meat to eat from the moisture as the member gets well and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to incise is that you look at where the apex of the abscess is, and where the sharp edge is; for it is never before; it is never behind; it is never on the right; and it is never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut there where the abscess opens, and its filling with sharp things; for you have the power to do so; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and take care of blood loss, so that the patient dies from blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of remedy
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there is a disease that is called "cough" or "pit", and the disease is old, and the remedy of medicines does not benefit, then the following remedy should be used: cauterize with what you will cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary therefore, when you have covered the eyes, that the patient should raise his head; after he rubs his neck with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then take away the patient's collar from all the cloth; then observe where the vein bites, and their roots are behind the ears, and they are well-established; then sign the roots, then cover them both with a spatula with two handles, as long as the cut comes up to the bone, and that of the back of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, remove the spatula from the artery and cover it on top, cutting as well as II do on the back.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is covered, let it continue to rise continually without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then measure the quantity of space of III hands, then sign the roots and cut up to the bone; and that which is necessary for the blood to flow out so it is outside so VI c/, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the repletion of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains on the bone without any discharge, if the cut at the absesses is not there, then extract the wound and bind it, and the cure with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of grinding
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient grindstone comes and catarrh is acquired due to moisture in the temples and old scabs and similar things, and it is treated by the methods of medicinal remedies and all that does not benefit him, let us extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is that the patient makes his hair grow again in his temples, and hears the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not too tight except in some people who are too cold; and if it is tightened, let the patient be stripped of some sheets, then rub the place with any rough cloth, and raise the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spanimal (an animal-derived substance used as a glue) whereon this form is based:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scorch the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then twist it upwards towards the pincers, and remove all the membranes that are attached to each part; and if the artery is thin, then turn it over to the point of the hook, and then cut off that part according to the quantity of II joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then nothing will remain whole or intact.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And twist the blood of the six joints up to three; and if the artery is large, then tie it with two strong threads made from silk, so that bleeding does not occur before the wound closes, and remove the excess between the two threads at that moment as well, and then, if you wish, then cauterize with a knife-edge cautery up to the bone as soon as the joints are cut; and this is the work of the surgeon, if the patient does not have a fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cautery is aid for ending moisture: for this is more great aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the place with dry cotton and place on well-made tents; and when you unseat them, so are cured with dry medicines that they give birth to char, and of tents, until they are healthy; and without a covering of the artery as long as you work, if you hasten to cover it by cautery, or you employ the place of vitriolic acid and strain it in your hand that the clot is strained; and if you do not have this present, put on the place your thumb until the clot is frozen, and raise the place of cold water until the clot stops, and be extracted as it should; and that which is muddled and lighter in extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein sharply from both sides, but let the sharp part be well spread so that it lasts longer in heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too soft, if it retains its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two tools an inch of space, and then when you have signed with an edge of the two, and you put a sharp instrument burning until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they are distant between the two joints because it is not souded of this fire instrument from all to all; and this is the form of the instrument:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes run down from the veins that are on the top of the head of force, and it does not benefit from the medicine that I make, and you see the face of the patient turn black, and feel or tremble so as to fall; and if they are too soft and moist so that the hair of the papers falls off, and the papers are burned, and scarred by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to have this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the ancient "curing contusions", and that is what you do to the patient who has this disease in his hair or forehead, then make III slashes on the forehead evenly according to its length; and one of the slashes is also like II dows all along the forehead down to the nose, and the others II are on the sides above the bones, and keep away from cutting the arteries that are on the sides above the bones; and remove your hand from the continuation of the two mandibles, and each wound has III units according to the joins; and have laid a piece of sponge and a lot of drapes for it to wipe off the blood, then pour the spatumil from both sides because this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.
