мãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмãмã
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	And then take by the side the oil of spices or another wet in oil with a lot of honey, and bind with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are of our time, let us put on the komijn with a lot of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the magda cannot enter into the oil by its hardness, because there are some men whose hairs are too hard, so it is that you squeeze the instrument which is called "alberit", from which this form comes:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so then break the conjunctive completely, and do not go too deeply, but make it thin, and pour on magda as we said; and at the end of the work dress it in the dark coming room, where he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and let him be free of all movement, and tie him according to its disposition for three days; then take off it in that very dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put him back after seven days; and it is not necessary that you do this in the hour of the cure or afterwards now, but it is necessary that you prepare this, because he will come suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	As the septimo day comes, you shall loose the oil before the septimo day, and address it to the one who assuages the aposteme; and when it is appeased, if thou loost the sight and putteth on a blindfold for any day, and be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then from the house little by little, and turneth to his case; and knoweth that no disciples must meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And then one came to us who was from the Land of Yrach, who told us that in our land it is done all magically, because it sucks the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our country, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	These are the shapes of almagda, so that he who does not know them may see them; and let them be of fine brass.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this middle subtility be, and behind it in three angles aigu.
de la char sor le neis	for the fire cautery on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Now there are times when they give birth or nas or char different ajusted, so that there are those who seem to be scorpions at the root of the foot; and if there is one of them or he has a char enchaned by foxy color, and if it is char with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these chars which is souef and not enchaned, it is convenient that you make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and operate his nostrils, and pour the oncine on those chars, and deal them with force; because you can hold it at the spatumile subtil agut on one side, as long as you know that that char is all ostee.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains nothing that cannot be covered, if he opens all the subtile and light instruments legierement, so that nothing stays; and if he does not rise up again, or incised in an apoplectic fit or as it should; and if it is apoplectic malignities, if you hurry and cauterize as soon as possible until the sinews are staunched and all the chars are ostee, then pour or birth easily and acutely or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the baby is sick, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is healthy; and if moisture does not pass through in this way, know that there is no room for the tool because the bones are crushed: then it is necessary that you put a piece of linen thread, a little thick, and tie it with your hands, and leave some space between each knot or more or less; and let the patient bite the thread with his teeth at his strength, and draw in smelling until it comes out through his nose into the mouth; and many times do this to the child when he goes to school, and it is a light thing for him who does it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know which one comes after which in smelling as we do with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it as long as you know the new has corrupted the plant, then take the root, wash the blood, and moisten the root with Egyptian unguent, and set it back in place right away; make it three days or more, as long as the unguents corrode whatever is delayed from the plant; and then put a plug of plaster into the nostril for some days until he is well, and if it is necessary to use medicines dried up, do so; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, as one distils oils and medicines into the nostril:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be of silver or gold, resembling an open lantern, like a plug, and conduct it also; and if you see, make a closed plug, and be the instrument plain for purging the head; and I often hold the head when oil or any liquid is heated.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder from the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee "telul", et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu'il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l'oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s'on le tarde a coper tant qu'il soit grans, si pren warde s'il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c'est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostèmes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxi color, et tu vois c'on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	as the newborn is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is known that when a solution of continued nature enters one of these cartilage joints, it does so only slightly, for fear in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, let one be carefully considered that, if a wound is fresh at all its sap, and then two lips are tied together with a stitch, and then he is healed as long as he is well; and if the lips are torn on one side or the other, it is necessary that you scrape off all parts of their flesh until they are healed, then tie the two lips together with a stitch, and tighten them, and powder on top of powder from dragon's blood, and incense burned; and put on the powders a piece of plaster of strength or another plaster always, and let it be as it will come out by itself, then cure it with ointment as long as he is well.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to stitch: you assemble the solution either with needles, as we said in the abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, in the mouth, there is a hard aposteme, resembling grains of sand, small and large; so you should return the lips, and cut each notch, and pick it up with tweezers and cope it in each part; then employ the fire after the application of vitriol, until the wound is dried; and then let it be clean, and cure it from dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the gum char is removed by tweezers, which the old man calls "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold it with pliers, and cope it at its root, and let the blood run or the wound; then put on the fire vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if this gum returns after the incision, and many times happens, so you cope it again, and cauterize: if it does not return again after cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for coping.
des sordens	of disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No disorders should be placed in the mouth between the teeth, those which are ugly and rough; nor should the teeth be black or yellow and rotten, until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so that you place the sick person between your hands, and his jaws in your palm, and remove the teeth or roots as long as there is no delay; and thus do with black and green, and yellow and other colors, until they are all removed; and know that the teeth need different kinds of tools to be removed, according to what the work requires, because the blade used for removing the teeth has a different shape from the one used between the teeth; and these shapes should be ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you pull it as soon as possible because this should not be done at all; for this is a very high-quality substance up to the point where there is no excuse for not pulling it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Now when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain about the tooth that needs to be pulled.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain forces the patient, and he believes that it is a good tooth, and he makes it pull the good tooth; but nevertheless the pain does not cease for this, until we have often wanted to do this to these gentlemen; and when you are sure about the tooth that needs to be pulled, then you must scratch around the tooth with a sharp blade very gently from one side to the other, again and again, until it is well loosened, then you tighten the blade very firmly; and be the head of the patient in your lap, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not fall out, take any of these instruments and put them gently inside each part, and move them as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the root is pierced and swollen, you should fill it with gauze where it hurts; and if you hold it taut with forceps so that it does not break when you remove it, and carefully wash around the gum to pull out the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure that you do not break it, and leave a part of it behind, and return to the patient with greater pain because of the root's mischief than from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be sure that you do not do so as the ignorant doctor does, who often by his haste and impatience breaks any carriage, and does not administer anything but what we have mentioned; but brings about a great disease for the roots to remain, or for the carriage he breaks, as we often wanted; and when the root is pulled, if you wash it with wine or acorn water or vinegar; and if that does not help, if you cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that the teeth do not break, are long points and large handles, so that they do not bend when you draw the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large members so that they do not bend when drawing, and made of good iron, and toothed so that they can hold fast.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root moves when drawing, you must put cotton wet with oil on the jawbone or iij.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the jaws are soft, for then the pliers that are called "algefri" seem like a tooth; and let them be made like a file inside, for this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, you must uncover the jaw completely around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", that is to say a chisel, which is this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be thin and big so that it does not break, and the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, from which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has II rings, from which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front in the razory of the teeth, and this instrument which seems a pair of large pliers, from which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and let this instrument be apart from that which cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtilely choose their own instrument according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are many diseases where the old do not teach instruments for the diversity of them; and if it does not break the cart or other bones, on which it lies, if you seek the instruments that are appropriate, as I have said, and help yourself with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be big and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but he can hold and remove; and then return him his place of medicines fitting for him, and if there is putridity in the bone, and it is small, then the surgeon has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear to be out of place with respect to the natural position of the jaw, and their shape is ugly, especially in young women, you must know that the root is not in its proper place after the tooth has come out, and it is not in its correct position, and he cannot sew or file them: then cut; and if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small pick, and which is made of iron obtained from one piece:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap is cut and cut with your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a file like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime where one makes needles; and when the tooth pokes and pokes slightly with the hand lightly, so that it does not move until it chimes; then the plane at the end to any razor, and its handle is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, so it is necessary to sharpen the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth moves away from the jaw
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth move forward from the jaw, either by percussion or by grinding, and the patient cannot press upon anything that he chews unless he chokes, and you have cured them with restringent medicines, then it is necessary to restrain them with a gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold threads never move; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick according to the space between the teeth; and if you notice any gaps between the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then insert the threads between the teeth, if there are one or more gaps, until you reach safely the healthy tooth on the other side; then restart the wrapping until you reach the part where you started, and hold your hand gently and safely, so that it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the bones of a bird and fix them with nails, and join them together, and put them between the two teeth, and place them so that they do not cut the tongue; and then leave them in such a tight position as long as it can hold out, and if they fall or the wire breaks, fasten them with another wire; if it holds out and serves in this way for all its length, and this is the form of the bones and the shape of the joining of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then if the tooth breaks, put it back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not skilled and patient should attempt this, and never make the shape of a tooth from the bone of a vulture, and put it back in its place where it has fallen short, and fasten it as we have described, and it will hold out and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the rings of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No times is the ring which comes from the tongue or nature, that he does not thus; or by accident of a seared sore; and the ovraiges are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and hold his tongue; then copper the nerve on the side, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or no, and this is of a sudden wound, then bite the ring and copper the nerve; and guard that the cut does not become too complete, for the artery which lies under. And when you have done so, then raise the water rose and thus, or cold water, and then put the tongue on a piece of linen; and wrap it around the sick person every night, so that the ring cannot harden.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the pain comes, let it be put on the vitriolic, and if it does not go away, let it be cauterized with the slow cautery, which is good for that; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a small red or black or hard spot that the patient feels but does not touch, for it is leprosy; and if it turns towards blenchor and there is moisture, then dip it in onion juice, and wipe it with a thin sponge, and deliver it from one side to the other; and if it does not go away to your ovraige, put vitriolic on it until it is dried up, and then return it to your ovraige as long as you draw it all out; then raise it up from there and from here, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	of the throat come forth from within what are called “goads”, and they are called properly the II amandres; and when you cure them, if as we have said in the division, they are not healed, let it be careful: if this is an abscess of small size and red color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either for fear of blood loss; but leave it alone until it has died down, then you will take it away, or else it will burst on its own; and if it is a pale color and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it over, but first see that the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then you shall set the sick person before the sun, and his shoulders be in your care, and he opens his mouth and puts his hands together between his teeth, and presses the tongue all over the instrument, so that this is the form; and it should be of silver or gold as well as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if take the knife and put it in the amber, and treat it above you can; and do not treat any threads with it, then the cap to the instrument, where there is the form, which seems strong; and yet the chiefs are curved, and one place another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or a hammer:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take the cap with pliers, where there is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be two holes on either side; and when you have kopë one of the amber, if kopë the other according to the same way, and then cut with a sharp knife, gargle the patient with hot water, and cool and easily, and if there is no blood coming out, then gargle the patient with water or cooked apple cider or oak leaves, and similar things, until the wound has stopped bleeding; then care for him until he is well; and do not cut in the throat any other abscesses than the two amber, if they are kopë like them.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman with an abscess that was located within her throat, which is to say a small-sized abscess; and I had it well sealed up the whole way down her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway that was stopped up, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she had delayed for even another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had been misaligned by two rain-sized passages through which the patient had breathed.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then hastened, and inserted an ounce into one of the two passages through which she had breathed, and then pressed hard, and inserted a large portion of a bow; then refitted another in the other passage where the abscess was located, and pressed her tongue; after that I inserted the ounce into the abscesses, and only let out a little blood; and so the passage in her throat became unblocked, and she began to drink and drink again, and did not stop cutting at the abscess for a long time; and the abscesses refilled with pus, and filled the space that I had left empty, until it got very big; then I inserted an ounce into it, and cauterized it within her throat: so she stopped growing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the pain comes from the eye, and it goes away and gets far away, then it is called "transverse"; and if it is large and round, then it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the healing does not benefit, and you see that the eye apostemes are pacified, and they are thin, then you should cut them out; and the one that is round and assembled and is not far away; and it is bloody or of a reddish color or black, then you should avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the eye disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blueness and remoteness, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument which we have mentioned above; then insert the needle into the eye, and twist it, and cut with two tools that I have said in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it will hurt the voice and the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two mandrels, and cure until it is healthy.

Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez. de la sansue de la gorge	And be the instrument curved to the tongue so that it can enter the throat more easily, and lift the tongue high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not come to the tongue, nor does it push the bone inside; and be sure that the patient swallows the instrument, for as long as he swallows, he should move or what is happening there; if the drink goes down, or he pulls the instrument back equally, as far as it goes.

li chapistres des apostemes	the capsules of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearance of the abscess capsules, as described in this text following various chapters of this book, and their diversity are due to two main factors: one is their shape, the other is the moisture they contain.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	The second type are those where the location is affected.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the abscess at the top is different from that at the bottom, and the abscess at the charn (the jaw) is different from that at the joints, each has its own characteristics in terms of appearance.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	If an abscess does not need to be pierced as it is not causing pain, then it should not be pierced at all; but if there is pain and it is a specific type of abscess that needs to be pierced when it is full, otherwise it will not be cured. For example, an abscess in the jaw joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses arise from the joints, and are left until they putrefy, there is a risk that the ligament and nerve of the joint may rot, which causes contracture in the limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is on the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the main limb; or if it is on the fundament, let it be pierced in such a way that it does not rot completely, and so that it does not break out inside, and come to a fistula; and cannot heal very well.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the right time for perforating the abscess that is dead according to completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the sharp edge of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is right that you should make the perforation where the abscess opens most deeply; and let the perforation run long along the neck, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equal, where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where they bleed, by what member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, if it is necessary that you leave the piercing until it is confirmed in the completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, if you prolong the course of the venoms from it, and there is much dirt; and by chance it hardens the lips and deepens its pit.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to which the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many splits according to the appearance of their size; and if there are such that they need to be chevered, and covered; when they have become as soft as cloth, and are numb, do so as you do with blisters: and if there are any that are split in three places, and if there are any that are kopé like the leaf of mirth, as if they were abscesses of the angles; and if there are any that are made into a round size, and other sizes and a semblant copée.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess on the surface, it is necessary that you pierce it clearly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has a large amount of pus, and you pierce it, if you do not remove all the pus at that time, but remove some part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then remove nothing more; repeat this many times with great care, until the pus is completely removed; but if the patient has little strength, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old people who are decrepit.

des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly inside its rib cage, as the lump and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Of those that are of good disposition at the back, and have the color of the flesh, and do not move from one part to another, nor are they deep; if you should cut them with an instrument, and burn them from each side, and if you need to cut off the two lips, as we have said in the chapter of abscesses on the head; and do it little by little, and be sure that you don't hit the nerve or open a vein, nor are they very deep so that the hand does not escape, nor look too far forward, lest you hit something that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you open a vein or an artery and it does not allow you to work on it, put vitriol in the wound or some powder that constricts blood, and extract the wound; and leave it until the abscesses have calmed down and the wound has softened, and then start to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound has calmed, if you return to your work, until you have finished it; then, with your index finger, see if there are any small sores, and cut them and clean them out.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a lot of vein at the root of the scrofula, it only makes sense that you cut this scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it hang, without doing any harm; then cover the wound with old linen dipped in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you gather together the two lips of the wound and sew them up, so that there is no delay because of its abundance due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you listen to cover the root of it, and extract firmly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have an abundance, pierce them so that they die; and pierce them like this before mentioned, in depending, then cover with care and similar things, so that they corrupt those who are delayed by corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then heal it with ointment, keeping it clean.
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old said and spoke about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw it done in our land, and it is the script of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	A those who have squint, it is necessary that the slit in the throat which is called the "epiglottis" be removed; and do not seek help from anyone, for all the veins and the blood of the patient are at those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the hole of the vein, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis so that the strangle which comes from the constriction does not occur.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to split the epiglottis, that we split it with III circles or IIII a small slit through, between II circles or by the quantity of the slit of the syringe, not in the cartilage; and these are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis so that there is no vessel, and the blade is long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to all its length, and split the flesh as long as it comes to the chin; and avoid the blood vessels if you see none, and then apply the medicine as we have said; and it is shown by the section of the vein that jumps out by the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which one doubts about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound on the flesh, and all the coast is under the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce blood, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: Don't do this as long as the throat is completely closed up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the deficiency makes it worse.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And then touch on the epiglottis lest the patient cannot breathe and thus is saved from death; and for this command the senior person to leave the wound open until the severity of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four; and then he commands that the wound be sewn up and cured, until it is cured. And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took a knife and put it in her throat, and she also cut some of the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and I found her also dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and I found the blood which was issuing from it, and I am sure that she had not cut a vein or an artery but rather the throat, and her breath was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and sewed the wound, and healed it until it was well; and there came to the damsel nothing but she was red in the face, and returned after her condition; so I said that in the making of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	The aposteme is called "gastric hernia", and is a large apostema of a yellow color, and is very common in women; it has two manners: natural and accidental; there is no mechanism for the latter.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is according to two manners: one seems like fat us, and the other manner seems like an apostema that comes from us of the artery; and there is fear, and it does not at all serve to operate unless in the small one, and test and search everything intramuscularly: if you find it as I said, like fat, and cannot at all do anything, then cut it well, and treat it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Our
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to describe ourselves, which I will now do; and it is necessary that I show the distinction between us and our functions.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a fever is a hot and fiery condition, until the sweating has passed and the heat has been driven out; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the right treatment, our body no longer has fever, heat, or pain; it is clean and healthy, and begins to resemble a ram, and becomes fattened; and are according to their appearances, whether they are fat, or dry, and of various colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat the body, you must first test and question all the instruments that are called "entromessoire", according to what their shape comes or the paste that is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for probing abscesses is that you press or more moistly place the probe in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little until you feel that the instrument has entered completely, then, depending on the size of the abscess; then remove the probed instrument, and take care not to stretch it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if the moist correans, that it be colored, then do so with this in the other abscesses; and if after the probed instrument does not become moist, know that it is thick, so probe it in a cross manner, and take it with pliers, and skin it lightly from each side, and watch the bag or where it lies, so you pull it out healthy with the nut; and if you cannot pull it out healthy, then pull it out by pieces so that nothing remains there.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	Car s'il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s'il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d'aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d'autres cures tant qu'il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and so the cauterized batans are opposite to you or other if you hurry and place the vitriolic paste, and leave it there II days or III, until the wound pus, and rest the blood-letting of the sanch; then return to the pot what was delayed with the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments that are inserted, and they are of 3 manners: large and small and very small; and there are 3 quarters which are called "albaret", and I which is called "breb", and there are also 3 manners: large, small, and very small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula; and also like the needles with which we cut sorcerers, and they are of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and they move those that are yellow, and they are more proven by black lead to encircle the borings of fistula; and they are of 3 manners: large, small, and very small, according to the quantity of the largeness of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the horns are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if to horns that have two curls of three ways also; and if to horns that have three curls, and are also of three ways; and if to horns that have two curls, and horns of a single curl only, and are also of three ways; and all these are necessary in their places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The forms of the horns are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if to horns that have two curls of three ways also; and if to horns that have three curls, and are also of three ways; and if to horns that have two curls, and horns of a single curl only, and are also of three ways; and all these are necessary in their places.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it no time to the place which is healthy for coping with veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never again do they swell the breasts of some men when they become corrupted, as if they were breasts of a woman; and they stay ugly and swollen, and who wants to heal them, if it should be according to this great form from this line: b. until g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scorch the fat, and employ the medicine by burning it in a cauldron, then join the two lips of the wound to sew them together, and heal it until it is healed; and if the breast drains down, and is moistened with its great size as if it were a woman's, if you make it into two ribs on top, by two apparent gaps; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the end of the other, so that the largest line includes the smallest according to this form, from this line: b. until g.; then scorch the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and you will apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, so that the patient does not rest, or because of the discharge of blood, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it drains the remnant and the fat, then heal it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	of the heels
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The pustules that come from heel-spurs are handled in the same way as hard scrofula with ribs, and if there is moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels that are in the abscess are emptied, then fill the wound with cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment from now on until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said in cutting scrofula, and if there is pus in the wound, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sewn together above it, then many abscesses form, and so do escaped veins and abscesses; and if you know where the artery is, then let the abscesses be long and perfect; and when you feel them with your hands, then feel the extraction; and if it is for a vein, then let it go away gradually; and it is foolish to stop up this abscess, and more so when it is sewn together with nails and hooks and where the collar and mouth of others are, and they are very big.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sewn together above it, then many abscesses form, and so do escaped veins and abscesses; and if you know where the artery is, then let the abscesses be long and perfect; and when you feel them with your hands, then feel the extraction; and if it is for a vein, then let it go away gradually; and it is foolish to stop up this abscess, and more so when it is sewn together with nails and hooks and where the collar and mouth of others are, and they are very big.
des apostemes des ners	of the nerves of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	So too do the nerves come from the artery and the vein, they come to the nerves when they are torn, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often with the shoulders and arms and in all their joints, and it is a painful apoplexy, and its color seems to be the color of the flesh, and it is in many states without pain; and when it is stretched out it feels good, and does not feel good all over, neither going forward nor backward, nor up nor down, and the one who is in the joints does not fit well with iron: perhaps there will be a contraction; and the skin at the forehead or at the top of the head seems to the spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the apoplexy is small, if it has a spasm, and holds it by its root; and if it is big, if it hangs on the neck, and the skin is scorched, then break the bone and join the wound with stitches, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	the large bellies hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	No times happens in bellies and ne other part thelul, and is a disease that is called "fungus" by the appearance of bread, and is the subtle root, and the big chiez; and there are small and many large ones; and I saw a man who had II or two bellies which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had little roots, and they were cut short, and they ran together moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I chopped them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI Z., and the ovraiges in l'incision so that you see that the patient is moist, and the color of the artole is blainche and moist and subtil root; if cope to the fire spatumile wide, and be in your presence cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.
