et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, dress the patient as you would, then place your hand upon the wound, and use a sharp implement to pierce the entire length of the wound, and close it up; and this is the common way to sew, and it is that you should use a sharp needle or more, according to the size of the wound, and leave a little space at each end, and fix the thread tightly with knots; and so one should treat large and small wounds.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine then it had been outside for XXIIIII hours, and the wound was closed after XV days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the miracle was that he did not die, and I did not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where there is none, nor any medicine; and I put on cotton wool II times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two ways of sewing: take the needle, and thread it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the flesh, keep the thread tight, so that the stitch is straight; then tie the thread off, and leave it once on one side, and pick up again on the other side, until the stitch is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which is properly done by Galien, if it is so as that there is a font where the two parts come together naturally, and apply one of the heads to the other head in this manner: pierce an eye or a head of wool near the mirror, and make the needle go through that part only, leaving the two heads of wool; then turn the needle, and make it go through from the outside part until it comes to the inside, by the two heads of wool; then make it go through one and the other from the outside part until it comes to the inside, in the two other heads of wool that are on the other side; and this is the muddled way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galien says this word, and no one testifies, that we must sew the belly to two needles, or each thread; and you must push one needle from one part, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew with corroded needles; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the sewing is more painful than any other belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as that of the other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just as the flesh has been moved, then bring back the intestine and the pit; then put on the powder with care, and if the flesh has been moved, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound opens again; and draw out the thread, and let the skin be sewed up, and the mirache; then cure the wound like the others until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to open again, cotton wool, and stir it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you have no other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will communicate with the main members, then you should wet another light one in oil of thyme or oil of rose, and put it around the joints, and wrap the bandages; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in the balls, and often happens, then let the black wine cool, and more certainly the putrefaction comes to the intestine; and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot be healthy when it is newly born, and this is because of the location of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and because its nature is close to that of a newborn.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the small intestine jumps out of the wound, put it back in the same way as you would an intestine, while it is still fresh; and if it has become old and has turned yellow or black, then find the location that is black, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the two bones, and hang them from the side of the wound to the far end so that the extraction can be performed when the small intestine jumps out, and the wound bleeds.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ripped and the wound is small, one can restore it in some places, because I saw that some very young ones were navered or stabbed by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was defecation and wind; so I applied treatment according to what I could find, and did not stop being subtle until it was healed, and I closed the wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	Et when I saw him stitch up, I doubted that the patient would be sick in his belly; and there was no evil, but delay in better dispositions, and feasting and drinking; and said none of the experimenters that when he has a little wound in the intestine, that he must bind it in some way: take a thread from great testicles, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that she draws her mouth out; and then he covers his head, and this holds so that he can't unbind, then puts another thread after in the same way as before, until the wound is all closed; and sews up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief wound is in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a thread cut from the intestine of a beast in some way: take the head of this thread of intestine that is well shredded, and then tie it to the head of this thread of fine linen twine twisted, then wind the thread around the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tear it back at the rupture; and this method of stitching with threads is good only according to the way of the fiance and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, most certainly when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no cure or medicine except fineness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	That said, all wounds and abscesses, once they have healed, are called "fistula" in general, and most importantly when they have scarred and closed up with a hair-like thread.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And the fistula is according to the green, hard and white nodation, where there is no pain, and it is also chewed like a peck of a bird; and it never breaks clearly, and sometimes thick, sometimes thin; neither does it break, and that I have spoken of in the division of wounds, that all wounds, unless healed, and there is no cure, are only by one of the VIII causes: namely, the smallness of the wound or sore; or its badness; or because it is too hard inside, and on the lips, which does not allow a break to occur; or there is too much scabs; or the place is rotten, and the substance is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for healing; or because it is of a pestilential nature; or because digestion and health are slow in that region, and run away by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or is necessary that I make you aware of the cure for fistula, which is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if it is partially broken, so that it comes to the principle member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are difficult to heal, and there is only toil and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to its principle member, and you have engaged to cure it, and you see it clearly, then take a tent of rawhide or iron, if the fistula is straight, seek it; and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a thin tent of pliers, for the pliers bend themselves according to the curvature; and if the fistula has broken hands, and you cannot find it well with tents, then cauterize it with your hand, that you know whether there are bones or nerves, and it is completely healed, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand on him, and the place where he feels it; and when you have really known the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cauterize it according to what I have said, and remove the wronged and腐敗的组织; and then heal it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from the right place, it is necessary that you cauterize it completely, as much as you can, then put wet tents in medicine water, and pour them on the top of the fistula until the medicine corrode the excess that is kept at the bottom; and then put oilements in janrain healing oil, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cauterize it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If in the nape or any of the main limbs you feel pain, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and darkness, then the king heal it as long as the corruption is all over the bone, then cure it with healing balms until it is well; and if it is not well, take away the bow as before, knowing that you have not yet reached the end: if you discover it and wait until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this does not happen, know that the corruption is too deep, so you cannot come to it; if there is no other injury but to weaken by nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it with pliers, if you extract it with the right instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all together, but do not leave one behind; and if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no error or fear, cut it and moisten it and heat it, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something on the wound that will cause irritation and leave it there for as long as the bones are deformed around it; and then the bones will be easier to move; and if it is a large bone, like a leg or thigh, wait until all the bone is blackened, then open up the wound again; and if there is a lot of decay and it comes down to just the marrow of the bone; if it is worth doing and covering completely up to the point of decay, then mend it so that it holds together; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg, so that you may use that as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was an elderly man of about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that entered his body, so much so that the matter came to his leg, and there was a large abscess, and he had no obvious cause to operate on; but by their foolishness they operated so much that it corrupted so much of the matter that it became a fistula, and it came to such a bad state that everyone's body watered and was covered with moisture from the trunk; and many times I saw him treated over a two-year period, and there was no skill in the hands of those who treated him until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines he had been given, and how it was corrupted by the fistula. The color of his body became red, and his skin turned yellow.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these apertures, and then searched all the apertures, and found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I quickly went there, and filled one of the apertures with so much that I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corroded and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone inside; I knew what appeared to me to be the bone's corrosion, and took care that there was no other corrosion than that which I had noticed; and I began to heal the wound with medicines that took a long time, and I could not join it together. And then I started again, and discovered the bone in the same way as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and knew it, and then I broke it open, and bent over the joint; but I could not join it together as much as I filled an opening with a palm of the bone, and then healed it with medicines. And he was cured and tightly joined, and there was no need to heal the wound again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car for the evacuation of blood often, but it was completely healed, and gave birth in place of the bone a hard shell, and was of good disposition and did not harm nor opposite from all in all, nor air nor come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the skeleton, then it should be done in this way: take a thread, and stretch it at the head of the bone that is open, and command anyone to extend it upward; and put another thread of another size larger than the first thread, and tie it above the shell that lies over the bone, and loosen the shell, so that you pull off the rotten shell, and uncover the shell on the place where you see or feel the corruption, and do so again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the nose is corrupted and does not open at all, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole nose; then put a hot coal on it, and then string the corruption from one part to the other, and let the string come out of the long part of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cover the corrupted joint, and tie the bone where it is on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other pain but that of covering; and if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or at the knuckle of the foot, then this is very painful, but nevertheless you must inquire about this corruption, how it opens; and purify it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not oppose you; and know that the incision and the strings for covering these bones are many, according to the sit of the bones and the appearance of the bones, and their thickness and subtility, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and for this it is necessary to arrange each instrument for each appearance of operation, and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; and imagine the instrument which you have need according to what seems right.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the dislocation is caused by heat, or if it is due to a fall; and when you have applied medicine to that corrosion, and it does not benefit, then cover that member up to the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes from this life, or from evil, which is greater, of the failure of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, so that they seem to be burned by fire, and the corrosion moves from one member to another, taking hold everywhere; if you hurry to cover it up, and if it is due to the percussion of certain poisonous creatures, such as sea scorpions and spiders and others, then the corrosion comes to the head of the two bones, and you cover it, and do not give it space to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes up to the hand, then cover at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cover at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy but the quantity of its virtue; and do this whenever the corrosion comes or goes: if it comes to the first joint, then cover after the other joint; and if it comes or goes up the leg, then tie the member tightly at the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is nothing left for the patient but death; and the way of covering or sewing the member is that you bind it above and below with linen strips, so that the cloth does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the patient another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et si the decorremens de sanc comes when you operate, if you cauterize the site thoroughly, or you put on some powders that restrain it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healthy; and I will tell you what happened to the patient at home in some detail: he got a blackness that seemed like fire burning, and this corrosion came first in order from the foot, so much that it stained all the foot; and when the honourable man saw the corrosion, if he covered up the foot with lead, he got well; and a long time after the corrosion returned to the place of the hand, and came to me, and I put on him things that cause percussion after the purification of the body, and I could not stop the corrosion; and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I did not want to do that, for I had hope of recovering the material; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, because the virtues of man are weak; and he became despondent and returned to his land, and covered up his hand with lead, and got well; and I only told this story to show what should be done differently, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No one time comes abscess in the flesh, and lingers so long that it forms a great boil; then bursts and leaks, and leaps forth as a bull leaper, and lingers like a serf; and the skin which is above is also thin as a drape, and does not corrode at all until it reaches the bone or the nerve, and such a disease is called "health", and is not called "fistula"; but when it is so long that it comes to the bone by a perfect hole, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin which is above is also thin as a drape, and does not corrode at all, like our drapes; and does not burn for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are sure that the skin will be infected, and corruption is not complete, and the skin is as thin as a drape, and does not burn at all, like our drapes; and does not corrode, take this medicine made of Egyptian herbs which is made thus: take oil and saltpetre and iron, equally, and put the herb in a vessel with fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes thicker as well; and then take it according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and clisterize the breast, and draw out the pus; and leave the medicine there for two hours, and then drain it by squeezing it; do this many times, until the breast is very white, and the wound is healed; and never clisterize with water of ashes when this medicine is not present, but take ashes from a vine's stalk, and pour water on them, and then let it flow, and clisterize it, until you know that the breast is very white; and if the patient cannot bear the pain, nor the Egyptian herb medicine or water of ashes, if you clisterize with honey and wine which has been made sweet, because the sweetness of honey has the property of whitening and washing, and the wine makes the patient feel better; and when you have done this, and are sure that the breast is very white, then clisterize it with what is born of char in it, and is that you squeeze plaster, and make it with oil of roses and wine; or clisterize it with some medicines and herbs, of which I have spoken, or treat with herbs; and if the wound is too large, and the caustic does not enter, then widen it a little with an iron, and put it in a tent of the Egyptian herb, or basilicon herb, until it is widened; and if the wound is too wide, so that the caustic can't get in, and if the hole where the skin comes out is above or below, cut or lower it to the place where it should be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the breast is fully developed, if it does not hang down; and if you cannot cover the nipple as you see fit, then arrange it in such a way that the breast hangs down to its lowest point, for when the breast is fully developed, if it does not hang down, and if you cannot cover the nipple as you see fit, then arrange it in such a way: that the breast hangs down lightly flowing, leaving nothing of the breast uncovered; and take medicines that strengthen the milk production on top of the breast, and wrap them in linen sheets that cover the whole breast; then bind tightly around the armpit at the wide end of the nipple opening, because ointments should be applied to the other sheet according to the quantity of the opening, and place it over the nipple opening to tighten the breast, and do not remove the large sheet for after many days once; and the one who is on top of the nipple opening often removes to loosen the breast, and know what runs from the breast, whether it be poison or milk or enough or digested or undigested; and take care that the patient feels pain or no pain, and if there is an abscess or not, and how your medicine has spread in such a way that you see the nature that rises over the nipple opening, then know that the breasts are already firm, and come closer to them. And then remove it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you remove the wound, if you change another sheet, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if her breasts become swollen and uncomfortable after many days, know that her breasts are not yet ready.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison becomes evident after a long time, do not despair of health because health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some whose late healing of their wounds and those that do the opposite; and if breasts become swollen and uncomfortable after many days, know that they are not yet ready; and if they lag behind and are stiffened, take medicine that is dried in substance and dried in virtue, as if it is completed, for there is a great deal of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take care to dry it well and use it with rose oil, and rosé it with good red wine that is equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and in that same way make honey cooked by adding it to a mixture of honey when it has been extracted from the fire; then apply it to the breast, and never administer it without arnica, or myrrh and incense, and grind them together and powder them on the honey as I have said, and use them; and if the cure is prolonged, and this cure is not used, know that corruption has spread, and produces an impression in the bone, or hard members, or limbs; if he cures a fistula with this cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the toe of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	is a blister that comes out of the nail bed of the hand, or foot, or perhaps comes out elsewhere; and when it has broken open, and we do not take care, then it comes to be a blister, and burns and stings so much that it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps reaches all of it; and there is corruption until the bone, so much that it hurts strongly, and the two sides are wide apart, and the color turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that has been reserved of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail is pressing upon the flesh, and beginning to hurt, and blisters, then you must put on the root of the nail what stops the nail from pressing upon the flesh, and cut it off high up, and carefully and lightly cut off that bit of skin, and put on top of it burning and corrosive medicines to kill all of it; and then treat with oil until it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	Et si la corrosion est dans l'os, alors le traiter avec force, car tant que l'os est corrompu, il ne peut guérir ; et si tu vois le os corrompu, alors traiter comme dit ci-dessus, puis guérir jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri ; et s'il est blessé et douloureux, et sent une grande douleur, alors il convient de le guérir en premier. Puis couper l'ongle avec un marteau, en coupant à travers au-dessus, et veiller à ce que la coupe ne vienne pas jusqu'à la chair qui est sous l'ongle, car le malade ressentrait trop de douleur ; et s'il arrive, alors mettre quelque chose qui apaise.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	La douleur du sourdoit de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Le doigt qui pousse dans la main de certains hommes est entièrement charnu, et par occasion il y a un os, et jamais une ongle, et aucune fois la racine de la jointure nait dans aucun d'eux.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Whoever is born with two legs who does not move, and whoever is born with a double joint who will probably move; the size of the one who is chiseled is so light in some way: cut it off at its root with a broad chisel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Whoever is born at the root of the double joint needs to be carefully treated; if you hold him tight.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In whoever is born with an odd number of legs who must be cut off at the hip: first cut around the hip joint neatly up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and finally treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together in two pieces are those that, by birth or by injury, or by fire's scorching, or similar things, come to be.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you cut off the joint that needs to be joined again according to its natural form; and place between two cloths or drapes wet with oil and rosin so that it doesn't stick together; or place between two thin pieces of cloth, until the joints are joined together properly, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	She begins to touch any of his two with the palm, so handle it like this is right.
des vils	of disease
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The vis are very big wrapped packages full of superfluous melancholy, which come in many parts of the body; and there is more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should not give him any kind of purification treatment, and then cure it from the base of the nose.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron should be done according to two ways: one is that you handle it, and drain the black blood; and the other way is that you loosen the vein, and drain all of it.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting should be done according to this way: first cut the leg of the patient with a sharp knife, until the large vein is reached, then tighten it and drain the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can bear; and then release it, and order him to wash his meat with black ink; and start again with the evacuation and healing when the veins are empty, and dry for the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. And if it is seen bent and twisted and wrapped up together, and it is not straightened, as we have said, then it is necessary that you tear it crookedly, but not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And the shape of iron where one covers the vis if it is twisted, and does not cut, so that it covers the vein; and it is a large twist because if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but it is thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where no grass or trees grow, and in the ground where there is no moisture; and by chance it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and the pus that comes from it comes from within the skin, as if it were crawling and twisting between the skin and the corse.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that an extremely great inflammation comes in the leg, then the places change, and it begins to come out of its place, just as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that an extremely great inflammation comes in the leg, then you should wrap a piece of cloth around it from one third to two thirds of the way up, and cover it up, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time it comes off, if it is too long, cut a piece off and wrap it again, covering the rest; do not wrap it tightly at its base, until it is all out; because if you do, it will enter the chest, and cause an abscess and corruption there; so that it is necessary to treat it little by little, until it is gone entirely; and this wound is treated when it is five or six hands long, or a good length; and I have seen it come from a length of ten hands; and when you cover it up, if it raises or protrudes, and pierces all the way down to the bone, so that everything comes out; and empty the matter inside, and apply medicines to the abscesses every day, then cure it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never use this hand to cut in the joint of the foot, or there the foot, and it comes out badly, and from which rain is needed; then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The hair should grow between the hide and the horn;
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buff disease," because it often affects buffaloes; it is a small worm that arises between hide and horn, going up and down all over the body, feeling warm as it moves from one member to another, until it wears away the hide, and then disappears; and is infected with pus of some kind of humors, like worms, snakes, bugs or maggots; and one doubts about its malice, because when it goes through the body, and reaches the head, it comes to the oil, perhaps enters, and destroys the oil; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cure and extract, if you can only do so when he is: then it is necessary that you place the head above and remove it with a strong, tightly wound ligature; then pick it up and extract it forcefully, and let it fall into the tray perfectly; and if you don't, apply fire cauterization to him until he dies; and the greatest harm he does is that he corroded the oil, as we said; and if you see his head coming close to the oil, then remove the wax from the socket completely, then pick it up and extract it forcefully; and it is necessary to use the patient's washings of solutions of medicinal substances for the bad humors putrid, and sear with meats corrupting putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some members and moves from member to member; and I saw this one that I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to see a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; then after a while, I felt it rise as high as a worm does in the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as if it were alive silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain left that place, and went into the shoulder, and then a little later corrupted all over the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she was rotating again around her body, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how this woman moved her member from one to the other, for I have never seen such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Anyway, I have often heard that people with this disease sometimes feel pain in one place and then in another, but I have never seen it as with this woman; and I thought that perhaps she had a hard body, and the veins uncovered, and because of this constant windiness; and I don't see it according to this reason for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see how to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it comes out as we said, put the plaster on him and keep it in place, and then cover it with a bandage until it heals; cauterize the sore; and if you don't see any hair, make pills from rotten meat, serapin, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	They are various, according to their appearances and according to the colors of their feathers when they fly.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	There are different types of arrows, according to their appearances and according to the colors of their feathers when they fly. They have large or small heads, curved or straight bodies, and some have wings. Some have two or more feathers, some are bent, some go through the body in one place or another; and some arrows fly in a particular direction without breaking any bones, or without hitting any organs: the brain, liver, stomach, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she dies and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you free yourself from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after several dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely extracted, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the arrow pierces the bone and the pain is felt in the skull, and there is a fever that burns and a hot feeling in the ears and tongue, and spasms and confusion of thought, and vomiting; and perhaps it may affect the nose or ears; and perhaps it may cause loss of speech or voice; and when this sign appears, you should treat it, and extract the arrow if it has not already been extracted.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the sneeze when it comes is that it is near the left breast, and also feels as though it were stuck in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the sneeze also moves like a bird's wings, with short black breath, and coldness and chills come, and fainting: so one has no doubt that death draws near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a sneeze that doesn't involve the nose is that there is no foaming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's skin changes color, and he sighs loudly and shivers with coldness.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the sneeze comes in bed, then the little ribs ache; and there is great pain and sighing; and all the limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the sneeze comes from the stomach, perhaps there is something coming out of the wound that isn't digested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow strikes one in the belly, and it goes through the intestine without a stop, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow strikes one in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and goes away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if it is made of face and neck and throat and shoulder and ajutoire and spine and forcele and cuixe and legs, and the limb that looks like it, are safe according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it does not hurt, so that as I will tell you that it happened to me, do not make it differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me that an arrow struck one in the neck at the root of the neck: I tried it, and removed it from the other side by cutting off the fat of the ear, and was healed without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And throw a arrow that it enters into the fat of the oil of paper of the rope, and the arrow was recovered, and I could not achieve but the point toward the wind, and it was an arrow of great color of a Turkish arch, completely light without ears; the game was sane, and no bad accidents came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And throw an arrow into the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears; I knew the barbs, and I took care to aim well, and the Christians were sane.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And throw an arrow into the back or belly of a man, thinking that he would die; and then he passed 30 days, so his condition did not improve; I cut on the arrow, and engaged it, and shot it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you want to cut a hole in the chest or back, and the wound is sewed up above; and hold the arrow inside, and do not disrupt its natural dispositions, nor do you find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I know another man, to whom an arrow was shot through his face, and the wound was sewed up; and he held it in this way so as not to suffer great pain; and many others too.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I saw a prince's man who had an arrow shot through his neck, and the wound was sewed up; he was slightly inclined to the left side; and the arrow was all pulled out After three days I was called to cure him.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I asked him to try all kinds of medicine, and he did not feel it; but he felt pricking and pain on the right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of an arrow. I put on top of the plaster with a medicinal and digestive atrative, so that the plasters do not swell; and I saw the plasters of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for a long time, and resolved the wound quickly, and delayed it so that the patient felt the arrow inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the medicine that corroded acutely for a long time, until it was opened, and tested it, and felt the head of the arrow which hardened at the spot; then I strengthened the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the head of the arrow was clearly visible; and I passed three months, and then the wound healed so well that I took out the pliers from one side and the other, and it would not come out; therefore I ceased to be subtle and to invent methods of instruments, until I took it with pliers well made, according to what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, as I dragged it, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And I saw that the cartilage from the nose cannot be restored; so I restored it, and the wound was sewed up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Do you wish to speak of the extraction of arrows, so that you apply your cure to those things I have not mentioned, for the book cannot address everything; but master surgeons do well with a small number of things, and those present and failing, trueve nine work, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign objects which come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows are in the limbs or they are stuck, following II manners: or through the place where they enter, or through another part; and the one which enters through that place is a sticking arrow in the flesh, and never enters once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her wait until the flesh is rotten inside, and let the issue come out; and also if it has gone into the bone, and she cannot come out, if she waits like this for some days, and every day she makes a small hole; and then she jumps, and if she does not jump, if she punctures all of the thin flesh inside, until the flesh inside is enlarged, and then follow her.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow has gone into the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the lungs of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said can happen to the patient: do not extract it, but let it be even after a few days, because if the arrow comes up to the vitals, then it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if an arrow has gone into the bone only, and does not come up to the vitals, and the patient stays without a bad accident for some days, then it is an instrument to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck in place and cannot be moved, then administer hot tar, as I told you; and then treat the joint until it is healthy again.

The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should be done only to maintain health and ward off future diseases; and it must be done in one of the three veins: the head, the groin, or the base of the neck; and it should be done early in the morning, or at noon, or in the evening after eating, when the sign of fullness appears; and it should be done on the first day or third day of the month.
