Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n'a point d'oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc'a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc'a septime.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	The patient who is healthy and free from disease does not have a determined age; however, it is appropriate to begin treatment for adults during the hours of day or night, at all times, and it is not appropriate to treat children until they are 12-13 years old, nor women except those who have been pregnant for four months up to seven months. It is also not appropriate to treat the elderly who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone is to be treated, in any way, it is appropriate to determine the intestines of a light enema, if there is a retention of mucus, so that the veins do not draw in the superfluous foul matter harmful to the principal members; nor should they be treated who are too dehydrated from food, or who are alcoholic, as long as it lasts, nor ydropics; and one should not treat after a colic passion, vomiting, abdominal cramping, excessive sexual activity, excess work, staying up late, fasting, and anything that weakens the virtue, whether by weapon or dagger; then slowly the humors, if he is fat, because of food, drink, and medicine, if there is a reason for it; then enter or bathe, if nothing harms him, to gradually reduce the fever, and treat the hernia from the back with care, as we have said; and keep that day from work, excess, lust, and similar things; and be modest and orderly, and let the surgeon who treats you be higher than the one who treats others, and rub his arms twice or three times, then remove the hernia by means of a knot, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot stand; and then rub the surgeon's hand with his own hand, until the veins swell, and can be felt; then moisten the surgeon's hand with the flame of a small drops of old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein where he is to be treated, that the vein does not hurt and fail to be cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if he opens it for the first time, it is good; and if not, then begin again a little bit more of that place where there is swelling or pain.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if his arms are swollen and the patient hopes for it, let him rest for a day or two, and do not bandage the arm: perhaps it will swell up as much as you see; but, if you doubt, do not hesitate to treat it immediately; and if the wound is small, so that the pain does not go away with just pressing it, then, in that case, I recommend treating it without hesitation; and, when the arms are swollen, bandage them. For this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the arm swollen, then do not hesitate to treat it, and put a little oil on it, because it soothes the pain in that area, and is soothing in that place where the oil is; and administer the oil to each wound that you treat, to stop the flow of blood; and, if he also has tremors and faints, when he puts it on the arm; but apply it very gently when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if one comes with a large abscess that happens many times, most especially when it is not cleaned except at this time where the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and place a wet sponge in water and in silk a little warm, and hold it for an hour; and it comes that you do this after the escape of blood from the vein, and if it stays in its place after some days no color or green, so it does not harm him; and if you see, put on anything of aloe or mirrremade into juice of calamus, monstrosity, or similarity.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance occurs at the cleaning of the temple: so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of your hand, then this is the appearance of evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Skip then that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for by chance in the absence of the artery; but make it a dry plaster to harden the place, and then heal it with other healing, as long as it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And according to each person's quantity of virtue, and the color of blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it is red; and if you see a lump, let it flow until it thins out; and if it is too thick, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for those who are weak and outside, and have a need to extract blood, let them make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for those who are strong, do the opposite, and let them save themselves often, and let them heal by cutting across, not by stabbing; and this way of healing is preserved from the decay of blood and the swelling of nerves, and it is better than long healing without injury.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose course requires healing, give them moist food in apple juice; if they are heated, heal them three times or four times; and if they have a cold complexion, moisten them before the healing with juice of grapes, or honey syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and sweet syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he is ill to the point of blood loss, after the exudation of blood, it is necessary that he swallow beer and aromatic syrup and use other things we have spoken about in the chapter on the treatment of syncope for the purpose of evoking a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up his food or is ill at other times, as often happens when he is very sick, that he gets better little by little, depending on the amount of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre. Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he is sick in another place, he must get well in two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has blood in his body that makes the pulse feverish; if he has to draw out a large quantity, and widen the artery so much that he spits up food; then you must take all the conditions for sickness, and put your hand on his pulse when he is getting better, so that death does not come out of the vein, and this happens many times when the person is careless; and do not consider whether the arm needs to be moved or not, for it would be wrong; but leave it until he is better a second time; or you point the flame at the spot until the blood that is frozen in the artery comes out, and put a little salt water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess has settled.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if need be, drain the blood a second time, whether it is in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is connected to the vein at the base of the neck; for it is composed of the same blood.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way to treat this wound is such that the patient holds his hand in hot water until the feverishness goes away; then let it rest properly, so that the vein appears clearly, then sew it across now, not wide nor long; and let the sutures be close together, and just below the joint of the hand, and if he cannot move it, do not put it back into hot water, for we use it more in a fever than when it is cool; and the wound from this vein is more cured than any other wound, as there is no artery or nerve involved.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The treatment for right-hand salvature is very effective for liver disease; this is how it is done: remove the hand, and dip it in hot water until the vein is seen; then cut the artery with a knife at every joint; do not be too careful, for the nerves are all exposed and bare; after that, put the hand back into the hot water, if it gets frozen in the wound, and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated for as long as necessary, put oil and wax on the vein to hold it tightly together, and do the same for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment for left-hand savour is good for mouse disease; and do the same as I told you to do for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The treatment for the foot is good for all kinds of disorders of the body, such as diseases of the joints, and also for the feet and legs, old diseases, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his health is such that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs it on the vein until it stops beating, and lies on top of the joint of the foot; and the vein if it is at the ankle, and goes up the leg with much rain; heal then where there is more rain, or at the ankle, that it may not hurt.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are exposed, and heal it by turning as well as by cutting; and let the flame die out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot pull them out, put the foot back in water, and let the vein well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if he heals the wrong way the first time, start again the second time above a small hole, because the leg is hot; do not doubt about nerves, as we have said, and do so with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The legs of the sciatic vein are at the ankle, and its blood runs to the pain in the thigh when it is time for birth.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of this vein is that the patient goes or bathes, and strips off from above the ankle three joints by twisting, because otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, so you should move it in all ways that you can, and crossing over; and it is better to cut it than to twist it, for the blood is up, and it is very full of hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not open it, so that the rain of the leg that opens or closes at the foot, and turns towards the small side, and protects yourself from the wind; and make it run so much with the pain that you see, and then unlace the bandage, and put on cotton and hold it fast; now he is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	The suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or bone, or glass; and the suction is made in two ways: by injuring and drawing out blood, or without injury.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This text describes the construction and use of suction cups, or 'ventouses', in two ways: by injuring and drawing out blood, or without injury. The text also specifies that these suction cups can be made from a variety of materials such as horns, bone, or glass, and that they are applied to different parts of the body, including the head, neck, shoulders, arms, legs, and feet. It further emphasizes that this treatment should not be used for all medical conditions, but rather only when "all the body is empty".
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if because of the necessity of disease it is necessary to fasten, or by custom, if we administer each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each period; for there are such who, when they need to fast, become very heavy; and those who do not eat and drink, and become pale and thin, and have darkness in their eyes and heads, and a drop of blood in their mouths, and their tongues are gone, and they are thirsty for blood; and if there are such who dream, and see by no food or drink or death or similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and most certainly when it is the middle of the month, we order them to fast after three hours from day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The cure for the headache due to the temperature of the head ... which comes with the eyes, and it is not useful that this be done after the whole body has been evacuated; and this fasting is appropriate for those who are of a cold complexion in general or who have a fever, because it does them great harm; and it is not useful that it be done by those who have to stay up late at night, nor those who have a cold head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become dizzy, and for this reason one should put the cup a little lower down due to the doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And the suctioning of the neck is in place for the recovery from the headache and the base of the skull, and therefore it helps at extraction of the pituitous fluid, and at splitting of the larynx canal, and generally, and at repletion; and it should be gently pushed back, because if it holds too firmly, then there will be dizziness or upset stomach or pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And the suctioning of the neck is in place for the recovery from the headache, and it causes blindness and headaches, and strangeness, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place for the extraction of the fluids of the base of the skull; and you must command the doctor that he express his hand in order to put it on, that he does not hurt the artery, and does not cause a sudden loss of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windings of the mouth cause illness in the mouth and decay of the gums and similar diseases that are in the mouth; it is in the place of the taste buds of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders cause a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the arms cause as much pain as three veins in the arms, for they damage those large veins; and instruct the patient that he not too tightly bandage them, since their muscles are naked and prone to swelling and hardening.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wind that is on the back causes as much pain as the bleeding from the fundament, and similar diseases; and it is necessary that the wind be strong and dry, for it has a duty to milk well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and it would cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses of the legs should be kept open, for they draw blood from all the body, and are equivalent to the ancient pains of the reins, and of the marasmus, and of the bladder, and take away the floridness; and are in place of the two sophenes, and of the two cheville joints, but nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring on a paumosis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the ventouses is that you should first make them empty, and quickly suck, and then place them carefully, and move them evenly, and keep doing this until you see the red and swollen place, and feel the heat of the blood; then stop, and remove the ventouses, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are some who have a tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to cut once only, and to make deep wounds, and to suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if he is thin outside, he should hit twice: the first time to thin out the vein for thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if he is very fat outside, he should hit a third time; and when we want to drain blood little by little, we should squeeze it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to drain blood, let us start often; and if he is fat, he should be struck perfectly, and the end is such that the keur [blood vessel] is broken suddenly, and you cover yourself with oil of vitriols and dissolving: if it is in spring water, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in autumn water, of watercress oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is thick and cold, take olive oil, or balm, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person with the injury is old and has wide joints, there is no need to put oil on it, but it must be washed after the windification of rosewater, or cold water, or water from mulberries, or water from cucumbers, or porcelain water, or other things like that.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who are affected by moisture, if they rise in such water, or in water from myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those with thick surplus, they rise in old wine, or water from sycamore, or anise seed decoction, or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not good to be treated by suction before or during the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after windification, but when it is time to windify, then windify and when it is finished.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are sick with colic, and let them not be too hot and inflamed; it is necessary that they eat cold things, such as pomes, grapes, leeks, and similar foods; and drink small amounts, and ride a cart, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should drink honey syrup, and fragrant wine that is neither new nor old, and small amounts of food, and small birds and pigeons; and it is necessary to give some men triple or musk before or after wind, in order to strengthen the limbs; and make the body warm, but it is not necessary for everyone who is hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The venesections that do not hurt are those put on the liver, and on the kidney, and on the podagra, and on the belly, and on the bladder and the reins and the hinch; for this limb does not feel pain when it is put on, but it is done to draw blood from one limb to another, as we put on the breasts when the disease is in them; so that the viscosity that is in the limb is drawn off, as we fill the venesection with hot water or with water in which herbs have been boiled; and they are not filled together, and never filled with pure water, but with water in which there has been a fire.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup is administered to fire thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should be of two hands wide and half a palm deep all around, and have a small hole in the middle about the size of a needle, as for piercing with a needle, and made of wood or bone, so that it does not hurt the patient when applied to the limb; and in the middle should be a wooden or iron crossbar for holding a claw grip, and there should be both large and small ones according to the disease and age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and those of thin people from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup onto the limb: take the claw grip of wax or thread, and put it onto the middle of the suction cup across the crossbar, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then one places it onto the limb, and the two should be on the hole that we have said, so that when one pulls, if there is steam, and one removes the suction cup; and one takes the thread as before, and one renews it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of a ventose that has been contaminated with pleurisy, there is no water or hole, and it is only contaminated when it is completely dry, and is placed on the limb with sufficient force; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	In the case of a suction cup that has been contaminated with pleurisy, there is no water or hole, and it is only contaminated when it is completely dry, and is placed on the limb with sufficient force; and this is its form: There are no cups that can be used for members or that cannot be used due to their small size, like lips and gums, and similar things; and in leather of a horse, if there are two or three holes, and others similar; and the quality of using them is that when you find cups that are in clear water without danger, you take them; and put them into clear water, as long as they are familiar, and do not have anything in their stomachs; and then cure with a suction cup and then rub the member until it turns red, and put the cups on; and when they become clean and dry, if it is possible to use a suction cup, you put it on, for that is worth more after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	Se ceu non, si leve le leu d'aisil, et puis d'aigue, mout bien, et puis l'espreint; et se li leus saine trop apres lou cors des sansues, si moille i drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchies; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broie ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu'il soit estenchies; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu'elles s'aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If not, lift the joint from there, and then with fresh water, very well, and then press it; and if the joint is too far out after the neck of the sinew, so wet a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, as long as the sinews are dampened; and if the sinews increase, so put crushed vitriolic glass or gall, and similar things, as long as they are dampened; or you put on the joint half of peeled peas, and leave them as they roast at the joint, now they will be closed; and if you need more, take other sinews.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the translation of the provided text:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapters of this treatise are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are beneficial for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Understand, o son of a carter, that the fine horse is bathed in this chapter, which has never been seen in any of the ancient books, nor have they read it; and for this reason the science has been lost in our land, for I have never found one good one; and I know nothing about it, except through the study of the ancient books, of which I have studied much, so that I have dealt with the science, and by experience, and by custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abbreviated it at the end, and clearly depicted the shapes of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in these two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore appropriate that we say in this book the sums of words and the chapters where the sagacious mind places his understanding, and remains on truth, so that those who are tested may learn and understand this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twists or strain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to save the sick person from part and other, if anything does not serve you, so as weakness of the corsage, or ensnare, or old; or his boots are too cheap, or too often; and bitter chaps, that is to say, cold jouds, and char of eye and of chevrills, and do not drink wine, nor bitter gruel, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, as long as you have no doubt about a hot aposteme, or an expansion of matter in the member; if the sick person comes back to his previous government which he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken nose begins to heal, it is necessary that the sick person be nourished with meat that makes great fattening, or has viscosity, like cooked wheat in water, and rice, and beans, and peas, and dough of wheat, and eggs, and fish fresh, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For as soon as the heat is removed, the breaking must be delayed and postponed.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot easily be mended or restored according to their nature by the drying up of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, as the bones of small children; but rather, heal the broken bone with large bones which join the limb together, as much as it was before; and do not stop at all from its work, and for this reason it is necessary to grow thick flesh, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that there are different kinds of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture at the top is different from the fracture at the foot, or at the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes up and another that goes down, as when the chisel cuts, or as the length of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break at all a small slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each has its own tool for restoration, and the appropriate tool according to what comes to mind in one's place; and it is known the break in the bone due to the turn of the leg, and open well by the side, and press with the hand; and when there is no twisting or change in the shape, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there can be a curve, or a slit, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not move it with your hand but put it on medicine that comes next, and then hold it now slowly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that came in the middle, and there are the two parts separated, now put them to be even as well as possible, so that the abscesses come up; and if the abscesses come up, if he leaves for a day, as long as the abscess is calmed down; then he puts it equal to the mold that you can make it lightly and carefully, and know that the restoration of this one is lighter than the restoration of the one where there are pieces; then hold it, as it comes next.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if the extension of the two parts is hand or foot, or a small member, or two strings, or a string and your hand; put the member according to its natural form, so that when the broken parts of the members are healed, you remove by all means the additions in their places with the muses you can, and guard that through your work does not come to the patient's injury or pain; and well join the two bones of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well to the hand if it seems to you that it is not good: if it is well dressed, and do not strip it too much, and do not press it as those who make it with their work cause hot and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in order, instruct the patient to not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, turning or in any other way; and well guard that the member be so assured that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	Car when he feels no pain, not even a point, and the need to put him in a comfortable position so that he feels no pain; and you guard that he is placed correctly, that tortuosity does not come when he is restored; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that the broken members are diverse in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and appearances: it is necessary to wrap fabrics of soft and subtle linen; and those that are large, such as calf and leg: it is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard thread, for the wide threads embrace all the large member, and restrain it equally on all sides, so that there is no patch; then put light splints III or IV according to the member, and restrain it a little at every turn, and tie it tightly at every turn, so that you press a great deal of the sound part, then take another thread, and return to the broken part below the splint, and restrain it slightly, not too hard nor too lightly, as we have said in the first line about; then put between the splints of linen or fabrics, until they are all equal, then bind them well together, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or an abscess, if you put something soothing on the abscess, and let it be like that for some days; then draw out on your pegs, and they are half a handspan long in width, or from a branch from which they are drawn, or from palm leaves, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	And if there is a break or a breach, if you put something soothing on the break, and let it be like that for some days; then draw out on your pegs, and they are half a handspan long in width, or from a branch from which they are drawn, or from palm leaves, and they should be according to this figure: But it is necessary that the peg that one puts on the break be a little larger and wider than the others; and it is also necessary that it be as far away as it is necessary for the limb of smallness or greatness; then draw out on the pegs as you did with the first lieure, then tie them together with a thread in advance, as in the first lieure on the breach; tighter is better, less is not; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and of linen; because if the thread is thick, such as I have seen from the works of foolish people who make their pegs from twine, it is a great mistake, for the lieure cannot be equal if it is too tight, and it should not be necessary that it have less than two inches of space between each peg.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is stabbed by the nails of the stars after extraction from his natural skin, then put on them a cotton wool or another rag so that he does not scar.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise and the bandage is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to extract stars from all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it is not good to put stars on them before five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the abscess; and you should use the method of ancient embowelling to restore a fracture, a dislocation, and a torsion: and this is that you take flour which clings to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of water, and put on this confectio, not too thin nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common method of the embowelling to restore a fracture to many states, and most importantly to women and small children, for it is not good to be too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twists: take honey, myrrh, oleander, asafoetida, Arabic gum, and mugwort, all in quantities of X; mirth and aloe, in quantities of V; alchechil, in quantities of VIII; and reduce them to a powder, and mix them with egg yolk from an egg. The ointment made from this mixture is hot, so use it, because it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly and effectively, and is useful for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for healing twists: take mugwort and castor oil, both in quantities of X; myrrh and aloe, in quantities of VIII; acacia, in quantity VI; and armatic resin, in quantity X. Grind them well and mix with egg yolk or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones that have come out of place, to relieve pain and prevent injury to the tissue around them: take fresh cheesecloth and soak it in warm milk and oil, then apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	It is better to use poultices than to apply direct heat; they are good for calming a hot abscess, and properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of poultice to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves and leaves of the holly tree, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of poultice for healing broken bones and reducing the swelling of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violets, wheat, each one in part; grind them and mix with wine, and heat the members, or mix with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of poultice, stronger than the first, for healing an abscess that has become chronic and is healing slowly.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of marshmallow, flaxseed, borage, melilot, and sage, and flowers of chamomile and violets; each one in part; grind them and mix with salt water or sweet water or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it except tar made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it must be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on a broken member, to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to poultice that is good for wounds and pain: take flour and knead it with water, or feathers of goose or owl down, and linen thread, and twist it together, and make a poultice and put it on him.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then unloose it a little, and take care that the patient feels no pain or restlessness or swelling at the site; if so, hasten to unloose it, and warm the member now; and dip a light cloth, and an sponge in water, and dip it in water, and lift up the member, until the itching ceases, and the pain is eased; then leave it to rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, wet with hot water or oil, and tie it on a nut, as long as you are sure that the abscess is warm; and continue this treatment little by little until he is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is causing pain and inflammation and swelling, then you must apply poultices and bind it up, if it begins to heal as you have done at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the member does not come out as we have said, nor should it be released except after three, four or five days, and never leave it for more than XX days, according to what is seen, until the break comes close to the shoulder, then hold back more strongly and increase the tourniquet's tension, as I have said before; and if you see that the member is drying up more than it should, know that there will be no recovery; therefore, every time you release it, wash it with hot water, and let it air for a little while; by this work, then stop the swelling on the member, and carefully tear away what is wrong, that restore the member correctly: this is bad, and if these are fearsome actions, I do not see any other remedy than to make it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many different ways of breaking, and there are various forms, and the causes are distinct; for it has breaks that are made by the impact of a sword, and the jaw bone all the way down to the hip, so as when one is cut or broken; this way is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above, and this way is called "absolute" break; and there is a wound from such great or small breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact inside, or a split, or of the jaw of stone, or of falling on stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating break, that approaches the tendon that is outside the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l'os ausi subtil com uns cheveux, et est li fendure petite, et por ceui est apelee ceste brisure "capillaire"; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l'os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And if there is a wound in the bone that is as delicate as hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called "capillaire"; and if the wound is caused by a stone, or by a fall, or by some other thing, and causes the piece of bone to go into the body, and the place where the bone was broken becomes so bent as if a smith were bending it over a cauldron; if it goes into the stone.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by traction on them, and inquiry into the tents, and by the rotten cart that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is caused by what happens when you uncover the bone and rub it upwards, thus creating a black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, take care of potential accidents that might occur with the patient, and if you see no bad accident, as vomiting, loss of understanding, extensiveness, paleness, fever, the eyes getting redder and redder, and other similar signs and symptoms in multiple situations, it is difficult to heal.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a potentially dangerous accident, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone within fourteen days at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the foot, so that you hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue of the bone does not decay, and the accident comes which we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the tissue that covers the skull, so it is necessary that you split the broken part thus: and this is that you squeeze the head of the sick person, and uncover it over the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more than you can, and because of the removal of blood comes to uncover the bone, or abscesses, help him who has come, and is necessary that you fill the place with wet fabrics in oil rosin; and let the wound rest as long as the abscesses are calm, and be sure of the removal of blood; then begin to split the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you chop the narrow end first, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another in the same way as the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have different numbers of shapes, some short and others long, and pointed, and made of iron; and work quickly, so as not to cut the top.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, so that you pierce it at the back, so that you bring in shapes with awls, not completely through so that they go beyond the bone's edge, and should have above the tip a margin or a circle, so that it does not let the tip pass beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each comes to its place at the edge of the bone, so that you have awls for all the test; and this is the form of the three ways of making awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the bone is that you put the awl on the bone and turn it two times until you feel that the bone has been pierced; then remove the awl a little further away, and do this all around, then take the space of the bone which is between the teeth, and make it smaller than you can, and quickly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools that you have such as pincers, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the cervix nor the syringe.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, if you see that you have retained sharp-edged metal which comes from the bone like an incision tool, but it should be softer and more delicate than the other incision tools; and if it does not remain anything small of bones or scales, if the bone is slightly bent with the instruments; then heal the wound with oil and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way to cauterize is that which Galen says, which is more effective; and he raises it very high, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you discover a part of the bone, where the fracture opens; and so when you have discovered that part, you put on the end of this lens-shaped incision tool, from which comes its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and this part is wet in both sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then hit with a small mallet above, so that you chip the bone slightly all around, and take great care of the chipping which is behind; if it is caught to the bone, then chip the bone slightly, for the bone hurts greatly, and causes fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce until the skin, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, then let it be roughened again with a sharp razor, and scrape off the scales with a fine one of which you must have several quantities, to administer in each place the most convenient, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have a very sharp razor, and then a finer one, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other cuts and fractures, you must provide treatment according to their appearance; and this is a thing that has not yet been answered by anyone who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, you should take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and dip it in oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth, double or triple, and dip it in wine and oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not hurt the syphilis, then apply by turns a different linen cloth, and never let it rest on the wound for more than an hour; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the abscesses are well healed over, then remove it, and administer to it, as roots and flour of times, and powder of incense, and alchemical things, and similar substances; and make these things into powder, and put them on the wound, and administer immediately with dangerous medicines without taste; and see that the wound is completely clean, so that you do not leave the infection, nor do you let bowels gather on the skin, for as soon as bowels gather over the cloth under the head, if they corrode and rust, they bring great harm to the patient; because when you put something mordant on the syphilis, it burns above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take good care, so that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness comes forth only because of the medicine that has been put on, which has virtue, then you should squeeze one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue it onto the wound; and then treat it in a way that seems right to you until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.
