You know that the two bones above are never broken one by one, for each of them is alone, because they are two; and that bone is cartilage, and it does not break unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you should put your little finger or nail on the bone, and make it equal to your index finger at its end, and at the back slightly, so that the bone regains its natural shape; and do it gently, and be careful so that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if it is broken in the upper part of the neck, and cannot return to its place, so you put a ray equal to the head of a small stick on top.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if it is broken on both sides, do this otherwise, and hurry to restore the first day if you can; but if not, after the seventh or ninth day, when the abscesses have quietened down, then bind the neck with linen bandages from head to foot, if the fracture is on one side.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind the other with the other, if it is broken; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that one should moisten the bandages every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it must be that they are moistened in a mixture of ochre and powder of hollyhock, and then leave the bandage on, until the bone is hard and the joints hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never put goose feathers in place of tent canvas, and if they are soiled with sheep wool, and the breach is held, and blows the disease to others; or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come while you are operating, so that you put cotton wet with oil or a drop of aquilone;
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come, so put an ointment away from here, of flour of sisle and incense powder, cooked with henna of sheep's wool; then bind it lightly, not at all; and if the breach of the abscess is small, and it is broken into little pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments according to this; then sew the wound, and cure the things that have been infected, suddenly, as ointments and oils suitable for this; and if there is no wound within the abscess, then cure the tent, and put cow's wool, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not very deep, and it is not broken in two, but only bent inside, so that it looks like a hook, then one should handle it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is fitting, if the break is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the mouth of the sick person; and if the break is on the left mandible, then put your index finger of the right hand inside, gently push the break back into place, and make it equal with the other hand from the outside, and smooth it out.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the mandible is in two, then you should bring the two parts together, so that they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth is problematic, because of the break, then you should tie it with a gold, silver, or silk thread, and put it on the broken mandible, and put two double cloth thereon; and put a large carefully made piece of leather thereon, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it tightly to the jaw bone, and command the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, let it rest on the third day, and then put back what has been changed; and put plaster on, with powder from the mill with much ash or flour of wheat, after you have taken out the cerote; and put on the lighter plaster, and if the plaster should stick, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; often it is healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscesses burst, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not break a piece of bone; if subtile ostéotome tools are suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces of bone, and there is no delay at all, if the wound is wide, put on it poultices suitable for that, to promote healing, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Of the forceps break several times before, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three ways: or it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work so is when the break is without wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder joint that is broken with forceps; and the others extend the neck towards the part; then make the break even on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or knot.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	Et si tu as métier d'étendre plus loin, si mets desœuvrant l’épaule au malheureux une speire ronde de drape ou de lainne, et soit grosse selon ta nécessité ; et estantes et levantes la forcele, et éloigne la speire à ta main, afin que tu mettes égale la brisure, si comme il convient.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you have the ability to extend further, if you put a round staff under the shoulder of the sick person, or thick cloth or linen, and it is large according to your need; and raise and lower it, and remove the staff from your hand so that you place the break equally, as it should be. If you cannot take off the head of the staff at the end, for fear that it comes apart completely, it is appropriate that the sick person lie down on his back, and put the shoulder under one ear, and press down the ministers on the shoulder downward, until the bone of the staff is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break on your two sides, and if you find that it does not fit, it is appropriate that you split it; and draw the pieces out lightly, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, take off the staff from this instrument, to save the sick.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it appears like a spoon, and is not a hair, and is also as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has II heads, so that you see it, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, just as the cut of the wound that you made when you broke the bone; and when you are sure that the abscess is hot, if the wound bleeds much, and the cut is small, or if you doubt about whether the abscess is hot, then bind the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, if you dip it in oil with garlic and vinegar, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And if the bone has wounds and tears, this is how you should treat it: put powder from the mill and ash of the oven on the bone, and put light splints on it, and fasten a splint to the fracture, if you need to; then take a very thick bandage about a palm wide, and wrap it around the splints, and wrap the powder; then take a thin stake three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the top of the bandage is covered; and put the stake on the break, and tie the bandage tight, and fasten the bandage to the bone; and let it rest for a few days, and when you see that the break is holding together, and you can tell clearly that the stake is not moving on the bone, then release it little by little every day, until you feel that the fracture has healed; and it will be healed in about 28 days, and sometimes less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the dislocation of the shoulder: Let it be known that when the shoulder is out of place and does not move, and the limb has been misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient; then powder from the mill with a lot of flour, light dustings, put on a double-layered drape; then put on a wide and thin splint, slightly larger than the shoulder width, and tie it tightly in one place; if you employ such a lin thread, so that the splint cuts evenly; then hold it firmly in place, so that the splint does not move from its position, and check it every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten again, and make equal the splint if it has shifted out of place, and lay the patient on his side. And the shoulder will have healed in 20 or 25 days; and when this number is complete, then release it, and be sure, for it is not bone that has shifted easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out forward and there is no support for it, then turn it over, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the femur to calm down an abscess with heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The leg is never broken in the middle, but it does happen sometimes; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it bends towards the inside, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no support, and sometimes he vomits blood, and the skin splits open over the broken bone, and he can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lie down on his back, and put a cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs with your hands, and gently make it even in all ways as much as possible so that the figure of the bone is like this; then wrap it in a cloth, and place it on the bone with the plaster, or whatever is lighter, and tie it firmly, and untie it every hour, and if it relaxes, tighten it; and if it needs to be removed for corrosion or itching that comes to the surface, or pain or abscess, hurry up and remove it, and scrape off the plaster, and treat it in a way that suits; then take off the plaster, and tighten it again until it is well.
de la brisure des costes	Of the rupture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Saves that the rupture of the ribs does not come forth except in great thickness after the back and at the top, and do not bend much unless because they are pale; and the feeling is good at the investigation of them.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoring them is that you make equal the rupture, if it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the plaster on, and tie it with a strap, if you need to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rupture of the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels great pain and a burning sensation as if he were crying out, for the bone does not close the wound; and it makes him faint, and he has great weakness in his body, and the old ones have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some of those who serve say that it is necessary to administer meat that swells the belly, in order to push back the rupture by force.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We don't do this either, unless hot abscesses come, if they haven't yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have come, then let them come.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And say that we don't put cups on the place, to draw off the liquid, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cups don't attract the excesses to the place for the weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And say that we must cover the place with another dry one in oil, and put tents between the sides to make the area even, then let it be treated with the cure for plague, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain in the spot where the cloth is stretched, then doubt exists for the patient; so it is necessary to split the bone under the affected area, and to put there some tool to keep it in place; and then, it must be carved, gently pulled, and then the two ends of the wound, if they are large, and it must be treated with ointments until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses burst, so dip them in oil, and put them on the fire; and cure while the fire of that which is caused by an abscess, and be gentle on the cost where it should be, until they are healthy.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Once comes a breaker at the base of the neck, and there is no pain; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it has come to any, and you can see whether it will be healthy or not, if you notice that its hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick it with a needle, if it does not feel anything.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many situations; and if he does not feel it when it is held and does not feel anything when it is pulled, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is cured, if you put the cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you know whether it is healthy or not, pay attention to whether its muscles are soft, and to the accident that has happened to him and to the movement of wind and excretion without will; and when he is soothed on his belly, if there is excretion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is soothed on his back and he tries to move, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: do not work at all in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come from him, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you rub it with hot oil or oil of mutton as long as it is relieved; then put on one of the plasters comfortably and dryly, and tie it up with a string, and order the patient to rest; and do not sleep in the part where he feels pain until he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Et si certains os sont désarticulés, couvrez-les avec du lin ; et assurez l'os, puis joignez les deux lèvres de la plaie, s'elle est grande, avec une couture, puis traitez-la avec de l'onguent en utilisant du char, jusqu'à ce qu'elle soit guérie ; et si le chiés de l'os est brisé, ce qui est appelé le "chiés de la kowe", si vous mettez votre pouche dans votre main gauche, et le placez égal à l'autre main à votre portée, puis appliquez l'emplâtre et le bandage sur , si vous en avez besoin ; puis maintenez-le en place, et s'il y a des os désarticulés, appliquez la pression, et assurez l'os, et traitez la plaie jusqu'à ce qu'elle soit guérie.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	the hip joint fracture
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	As it happens that the hips are broken, and if so, then there is a little bit of pain in the head; and let them be long, and incline to the back, and come to the patient pain in the place, and stabbing, and swelling what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it as long as you are above the break; and know which is the break and what shape it has; and if the break is at the head, so make the break even, as long as it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, so bring the patient up by his stomach, as long as the restoration of that break is made known to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, if you put on plaster, then put on a beam of wood or oak, and remove the break so that it does not move; and engage the place by the sides, as long as the length is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscess hurts, as long as the abscess is relieved, and put on what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and hold it as it should be, unless there is no bad accident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder's adjutor is that which is between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of the two ways: which is that you take a strong rope, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And hang two chains from the II chocks, and tie them high up, and cut the patient on a scaffold; then have one of his arms broken on the pole, as far as it comes to rest, and take a strong rope, and then put it on some heavy object or have it carried down; then make the break even with his hands together, as far as the break returns in the way that should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one should send the sick person to his loins, and tie the hand to his neck, then order two ministers that one should tie who is on the brisurer to his hands, and the others should tie all his limbs, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tie the limbs all together, and on the brachium, and extend each minister to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the brachium is near the shoulder, then it is necessary to put the limb all together, and at the base of the brachium, and likewise towards the shoulder; and so that the brachium is even on its side, and even at the base; then make the brachium even, as it should be, and hold it, if abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the abscess breaks out, do not remove it until at least seven days have passed, and place a wet cloth or oil on it until the abscess is calm; then remove it, and the way to remove it is that you put the poultice on the break, then bring the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and wrap a blanket around it, and remove it from the break and from the arm so that the arm is in its place, if nothing hurts it or if the bone has not been broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use a splint, and put a wider and stronger splint on the break than the others, and leave two inches of space between each splint, and make each splint large enough to go over the break III inches on each side; then remove it with more force and less movement as I said at the beginning about the poultice on the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the star and the stringing, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the incision warm, let it tie up until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each of the three days the thread, so that itching does not arise or come to place, or the re-shaping does not come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the splint, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such an accident does not come, if only the splint is removed after three or more days, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and he sets the shoulder joint straight with a smooth piece of linen, and each hour checks whether the broken member no longer moves, or has become softer; if it heals by the power of medicine, and he gives him the food that we have described in a certain way, so that the food is at the first subtle level; and when it begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is fitting that the shoulder and leg should be healed in forty days from today; and then, it must be loosened and bath and medicine for healing should be applied to it.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the tightness is bad and blocked, if it takes one or two months to loosen it up.
de la brisure du bras	from the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosciles", one small and one large; the small is at the top, and the large is below it; perhaps one or both of them might break, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the healing is easy and good; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad and painful, and more so than when both of them are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small dark spot that is bruised alone, then what is needed is to gently stretch it out and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If it is the large dark spot, then what is needed is to stretch it more forcefully; and extend it on one cussin, and shade the pouchet of the hand further up than the others, and the small ones lower than the others, and so that the patient crosses over himself, and the cussin in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no labor; then extend the ministers of his arms to the part affected on his side, or his leg, and other ministers on the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then let it be made even according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is in pieces from the break, then let each one be put in its place, and if any of them grasp the other, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do so onto the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the cauterization there is a wound, I have spoken of it to the singular chapter; if he takes the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the restoration by cauterization there come abscesses, then I will cover them with a plaster made of oil and rosin, which is not too hard nor too soft; and I will cover them from above gently, until the abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then cut the cerotide, and I will put the plaster of the powder of the mill with much honey, then put the splints, and let the splint of the cauterization be closer to the arm or leg; and draw it up more than other parts, and always less on moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter of the plaster; and may the plasters that are over the cauterization be soft and moist, and not too hard nor too rough; and let the thread, from which it is drawn, be made of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And restore the member and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, as when itch comes to the member, it is convenient that you warm the member with hot water, until the itch is calmed; and let the member not be tight but rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the extraction, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone is dislocated, and similar things, then treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it should not come to the member because it is too tight, then you must make it soft a little, and leave it thus for a few days, until the tightening comes again, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the illness, then take off the shoulder for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or if he has broken his neck, then let him hold his hands by his sides, and let his necks be even, and keep them from movement and shaking, and sleep on his back; and know that this breaker is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	are often many breaks in the back of the hand and there comes but little pain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	When the palm of the hand is broken or cracked, so that the patient cries out and stands upright with his hand even before him; then put his hand on a extended cloth, and extend the broken bones, and make them even, as they should be; and put plaster and staples, if there is an abscess, then put a staff according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped in I sheets of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks in the garden between the root of the plant, then make a staff of reeds, and command the sick person to tie it to its broken root; and then extract it with a long reed, and be careful not to cut off so much of the plant from the hand as the plant from the root, and extract it, if so is fitting.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks at the end, then you should put a staff on it, and another under the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and tighten the bond between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if it breaks at one of the two ends, then you should make it even, as it is fitting; and extract it with the plant, and if you see that you need to put a small straight staff to raise the break, so that it does not move; and if the break is at one of the other two, then make it even, and bind it to the sound one next to it; or you can bind them all together, holding them tightly, or you can put a staff on it, as if you were carrying an arrow; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the apoplexy, and assist those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the chest bruise
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The rib of the chest is often bruised, and we can clearly see it move forward and backward when it returns; and the healing process is good if we bind it above the bruise and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then sets his ministers equally to his sides; and it is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the chest, then one of the ties is towards the thumb and the other is towards the heel of the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then one of the ties is to the leg and the other is to the heel of the break; and so put the slab with the bone in its natural position, and then place the plaster, and bind it, unless there are any breaks in the leg.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it cool then return to your work and your treatment; the time has come in some way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess, let it cool then return to your work and your treatment; the time has come in some way. The wound should be cleaned with salt water, and the surplus fluid should be allowed to drain, then the leg should be wrapped in a dry cloth;  a long bandage should be tied between the thigh and the leg, and the knee joint should be protected with another bandage; and then the bandages should be applied to the wound, and an armature of wood or metal placed on the bone of the leg. Then fix the bandage tightly between the thigh and the leg, so that there is no movement; then two or three turnings of cloth should be placed over the wound to protect it, and a turning of cloth should be placed under the knee joint, and the chief turning of cloth should be fixed to the top; and then the bandages should be tied tightly around the thigh and leg, and the cloth beneath the knee should be fixed in place. Then the bandage should be loosed slightly, so that there is no more pain or swelling; and then two turns of cloth that you have tied between the leg and the thigh should be uncovered, and the three turns above them should be uncovered, and then return to the joint at the top, as far as the foot can move; and let the bandage remain in place until there is no more pain or swelling.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, if it slips and moves away from its place, and moves the one that comes to it, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that hold onto it, then he should pull it hard, if he can; and if he cannot, then he should split the place, and tear it out forcefully; and heal him as we have said, until he is well.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the chest injured when we put staples there, as in the shoulder or arm; but a restoration made in this way does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the chest is restored in one day, or little more or little less, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of the ankle
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	And know that in the street of the ankle there is little injury, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is just a crack or a gash, and goes to all parts, and feels no pain, and this can be felt well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one should make even what is long at both ends, as much as possible; then put on the plaster, and put on a round splint if you need it, and hold it in place as it should be, then apply all the provisions we have spoken of in other breaks, such as a hot poultice and others; then put on whatever injury it is, as long as it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg break
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 know that in the leg there are II bones, of which one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and all other breaks are the same as those of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones break together, the leg turns around everywhere.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his subtle nose is broken, then turn back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick nose is broken, then one feels great pain and it can be seen well; and turn back.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then bring it out, and make it even, and tie the joints evenly; however, the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter; and align it according to your art.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, then take two thick hair of the person's leg on either side, and let them run along the leg from the ankle up to the toe; then wrap them around twice above and below, and tie them in the middle, so that the leg does not tilt towards one side or the other, and so is good; and no one should administer a balm to the long hair, and if it is rough, and put on the wound where there is pain; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident; and if the cure as far as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	About the break of the bones of the feet
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	About the ankle, there is no break at all, but from the bones of the feet there comes a break in some cases, and in most situations there comes only a fracture, and it has never been seen to occur on its own.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the feet, and you see these bones sticking out one above the other, so that the patient has to put his foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then now place your foot on their two ends, raise them up until they go back into their places; then apply the plaster and plug it in, and tie a small piece of cloth over the navel of the foot, then wrap several drapes around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even if they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if you restore them, as we have said to the hands of a man; then put on the broken one a stone according to its length from the two, and let it be a little wider, then put under it the foot that I said, and strain ahead; and if there are II or III or more, broken, then put on each of them a stone according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and strain the foot under the stone; and be on the top of the head of the foot the belly of the stone so that it bleeds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I said about the other breakers, when we have said it; and heal each injury as it deserves.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone of the knuckle
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the female nature is broken, if she sits enlarged, then lean her to the part of the back, and hold her behind; then fill the cavity of the nature with cotton, and put in it as big as I sit; then remove the woman, and lift her back little by little, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and bring the bone with the seat; and when she wants to urinate, if she jumps the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it down, and so do for seven days or less: then will be restored the break, and will die, take a bladder of lamb, and tie a chain to the hernia, and pour all the bladder into the nature; then blow in the chain form, until the bladder is gone inside: the nature will then come back the break; then fill with cotton, and leave it for some days, until he is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the man's or woman's jaw is broken, if he sets it as we have said in the hip bone; and these breakages are not hidden from him who makes his study and use of them, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaking means many good things in the right way of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an goose's neck and fill it with urine; then wrap it in a cloth and leave it wrapped for three days or so, and it will be healed by the hospital's means.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For those who have broken a bone with a wound, even if it is a large one, such as the hip or shoulder or arm, let them be healed now, so that the wounds that we have spoken of may testify to their healing.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but the vitriol burns, then, if you have nothing else, continue to restore the break in the same hour, or else the abscesses will come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses come out, but continue to leave it until another day, as long as the abscesses are calm and you don't touch them nor on the third day nor on the fourth, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the side that is covered with the wound, it is necessary that you place it at a slight angle with your hand, at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal so that you can make them the same length as your hands, take this iron instrument which has seven or eight inches in length and its width corresponds to the quantity of the wound; and because it is necessary to bend it three or four times according to what is needed in each cure of a broken bone; and be round and a little thick so that it does not press on the limb at your work, and be curved forward and thick in the middle so:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palanquin", for it is necessary that the curved shoulder be placed on top of the head of the visible bone; and let it be set once, until it comes back, and even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot take the bone well, you must chop the head of the bone until the instrument has the ability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, with a suitable tool, either an incisor or a chisel, within your power; then resect that which is delayed in the bone of roughness and small scoops.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone has been reset, and the patient feels great pain after it, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then soak the dressing in black vinager properly if it is in it; and do not put on any wax or other oil where there is oil, lest it bring about corruption and decay; and administer the medicine when you have restored the bone, leaving the wound uncovered, and cover it all around with the covering, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not tightened with the fracture; and many times this has been done to the misfortune, and have brought up on the patient either death or decay; and let the instruments be softer and more pliable than those of other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a worse accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it is not good to put on splints; but wrap hard drapes around, instead of splints, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days to the wound, if an arrow that you have put there has come out, and put on it a healing ointment, as healing tar and similar things;
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the arrow runs down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it passes, and he cannot hold it in place, but it comes apart again, because there are little pieces of bone, so that you must take the wound with a towel, and those little pieces of bone that come out cause pain;
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to light, or some other kind of corruption, then you must cure it according to what he said in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opened on a limb, as in the case of the hip or shoulder bone, and other large bones, do not draw it out, for many die from it, but leave it to rot; perhaps after XX or XXX days, then heal the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the bruses that come from the sudure
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Come often we come after the health of the break, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a ugly thing to see the limb's figure; and perhaps cannot make the limbs do their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that we do not break it again: if you administer stinky medicines, as in aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarcocollo, acaice, and others like them, so that you do not press any of these things, or all together, and confound them with wine that is stinky or with a lot of egg or with honey; and put them on the nodules in piles, and bind them well, and do not take them off for many days; and then take them off, and start again on another one, until the nodules are hard; or you put it on a piece of skin that is well made; because the property of the skin is that it makes all swellings on the limbs hard: and if the nodule has already turned to stone, it is necessary to cut it off, so that the excess appears; or you take it to any barber, as long as it is hard, and heal it as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member that is weak after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break in the bone has healed, and there remains weakness and tenderness of the limbs for one or more of the following reasons: either because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because it had too many bindings, and could not move the limb; or because of many wounds; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because there is a lack of blood in the body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat well and make the body tender, so that the blood increases in it; and give him baths, and provide pleasure and rest; then put wax on the limb, so that the wax attracts much healing, and rinse it often with warm water, until the healing goes into the limb; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two injured limbs after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb completely new, for many foolish people have done this in our land; but such practices are blamed, and great harm and perhaps death result. However, if the knots and torments are fresh, they should be heated with warm water, or soft herbs are cooked, such as foils of whale oil, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the unguent is made soft, such as a well-made hydrogel, and you take the musk oil of whale oil, and confound it with beef fat or sisament oil, and make an unguent; or you take fig pastes, and grind them with hay of colon, and similar medicines that soften the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the arm raised by continuous and prolonged friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make sure there is no movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if it is twisted and stiffened, as in the case of a bone, then it must be opened with the iron, covering up to the bone, cutting with a very light knife; and put on ointment and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now necessary to bring back sensibly.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one is delayed, and the joints swell, and perhaps he is put back in place at his own pace; because then it cannot move at its own pace: many times brings in pain and other pains; nevertheless, when this will come, let the sick person be made well, leaving him until the abscess is appeased; then raise the member with warm water and oil, and then move it lightly, and cure each member as the cure comes back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chaplets for the dislocations of the shoulder joint up to the edge of the breastbone.
des mandibules	the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	And there are two ways that the mandible should be dislocated: one is slightly out of place and a little soft; another is completely displaced and hangs down towards the chin, causing the saliva to flow from the mouth so that it cannot be held or the mouth closed, and envelops the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return it with several different positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must immediately reset it, without delay; and in such a way that the ministers hold the head of the sick person, and pour a little water from one of their hands into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, for there are two ways of setting it: and the other two hands should be placed apart to make it even; and order the patient that he softens his mandíbula bones, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the mirror be made equal, as soon as it revives in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And let it be brought back with care, especially if the two mandibles are together, so that they are heated with cold water and oil, as soon as they are brought back slightly; do not wait to bring them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed with a softener, if put on sheets wet with an oil made of rose and wax, then let it lie lightly; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor strive to open his mouth, but eat leichtily, as soon as the pain is gone, and the mandibles are healed; and then eat whatever you want, and do not try to open your mouth to eat or drink, until the mandible is well healed and whole.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset within an hour, and are not restored to their places, so that there come fevers and sudden pains used, and by chance stomachache, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then you know that it is a sign of death; and many die within nine days.
de la forcelle	for the fork
