Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not dislocate due to a lack of movement from within the bone and from the top, and does not dislocate at all towards the back, and one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and extends his arms; and then press the joint with your palm, and it will come back; then put on the plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the jaw that is toward the neck cannot be dislocated; unless, and if it does not dislocate at all, so he returns to his place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it, and command the patient to rest until he is well; and in this way the shoulder is also reset when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	1. That the shoulder dislocates only in three ways: first, that it comes out of place at the end of the arm; and second, at the top of the thigh bone; and perhaps it comes out of place at the back of the shoulder, but not; and does not come out of place from within towards the neck; and many times comes out of place towards the shoulder blade, but at those who have little strength, for then must they be taken to hospital; and at those who have enough strength, let them go back and rest.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	2. And perhaps it happens to some men that there is beating or breaking, and the shoulder becomes hot with an abscess, and they think that it has dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	3. So then you must test it out, until you are sure of it; and then begin the treatment.

Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches that the joints of the hip and the shoulder come only in dislocations alone, not at all as other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to IV parties: inside and outside, before and behind; and more inside there, and less displaced before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai. If these dislocations are old, and they delay according to their disposition, there is no cure; and it only comes that he has presumed.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those who have fresh dislocations, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to reset the joint, and it turns inward and outward, and moves to the right and left; perhaps it will come back, and there is no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, it is necessary that you prepare the minister very strongly, and hold the leg very firmly with two hands, or with one link that is tied to the knee; and other ministers extend their hand above in such a way that they press their hands down on their peers, then tie a string around a foot; and other ministers take the head of the line; and they stretch up and down all at once, until the patient has been raised from the ground once, and stays there.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This way of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	And if not, it is necessary to put the cure on his sound side, then place the link on the root of the thigh, and the string that is away from the ankle, then extend the link upwards towards the ankle, and upwards towards the force; then grip the arms of other ministers, and embrace the thick leg of the ill thigh, and stretch it in a line: so it will return to its place now; and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this way that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the sick together with a strong rope from the heel, and from the knees, and let the leg of the sick be extended more than the other; then hang him by the head on a post, and let his two arms be above the ground; then command the minister that he embrace the head of the chest, and let there be others who hang with the sick who embrace the chest well, for now the joints are returning to their hospital.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are away, so lay the sick, as we have said in that which has gibbosity, and strap the rope properly on the leg of the sick, and on the foot also; then put two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then stick one torch between the thighs of the sick in the form; and let there be wet drapes placed around, so that it does not burn the sick, then extend each minister towards him, and let the minister look at the dislocation equally with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place on a .ie. bed, and press as we have said in the gibosity, and lay the patient on the left side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are in front, if it is convenient to extend the leg of the patient further away, and according to what I have said; and make him lean his weight on the other hand, and press it down towards the ankle, then take the weight off with the other hand.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are in the back, if it is not convenient to extend the patient's leg further away, and do not raise up on the ground, but rather that he should be lying on his side as if he were extended as described above; and lie on his face, and keep the leg extended as we have said before, and press on the joint towards the table; and it will be complete when the patient extends his legs and they are even; then take off the bandage, put on the plaster, and tie it up with a bandage, so that the hunchback does not move; and let him rest for III or IV days, then remove the plaster, and make him bleat until the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward, outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his knee to his chest, and if he does not bend it to his chest, knowing that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his kneecap with your palms, and pull it between your two legs, then bend the II ribs of the knee cap together; and other ministers extend his foot, until the knee has returned to its place, and the signs are that he is bending his leg to his chest easily; and put the plaster on, and make him walk with his leg bent to his chest, and join them firmly together for III days or IIII, then let it go; and do not work the patient to walk until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, if you administer a strong extension, as we said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation from the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never dislocated, and never fully displaced inward or outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is displaced, and the bend before the part where it is displaced: one must gently ram it with their hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is displaced all the way, you must make the patient lie down right side up, and stretch it out on the leg below the ankle; then draw it up towards your hand, and then let it fall back down again; and do this twice, as we have said, stretching and drawing the foot; if it returns, it is good; but if not, then begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return, then make the patient sit on his back on the ground, and place a staff firmly in the ground between his knees, and tie the blankets around him so that he does not slip; Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is done, so put on the plaster and press it down, and let the splint form, and fasten the foot to the leg, and guard the ankles that are behind the ankle, so that the bonds are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and the bonds will become soft if the splint is left; then remove it on the third day or fourth day, and let the patient go away after four days; and if he goes before that term, there is still a danger that it will dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come up, so calm them down as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	The two of them.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, so it is a good idea to stretch them smoothly without work, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no place at the foot of the two legs, so it is a good idea to make the patient sit on a flat bed or on a table completely upright, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press your foot down until it has healed; and when it is even, and there is nothing open, so make a splint with a board at the two legs, then form the splint, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and let him rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	for wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	For wounds come with dislocation, and we must restore them, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not learned in the art and have not used it long, and if you are not compassionate and tardy, do not be bold; and use at first soothing ointments, and leave the patient to God, unless you see a chance of health; and when you see a chance, now restore the limb to its place, so that warm blood comes; and when the limb is in place, administer drying ointments, and if there is fracture with small bones broken, do as we have said for simple illnesses; and beware of going down the path of fear, according to what I said, because it will cost you much according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming and protecting yourself and your body.
Amen	Amen
